Definition and Types of Ada and Qada
Defines ada and qada with types and linguistic nuance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada and qada, identify their three types each, and distinguish between delivering the exact wajib and its equivalent.

Core Idea
Ada delivers the exact wajib by command; qada delivers its equivalent when the original is missed.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh introduces the two fundamental categories of fulfilling a command: performance (ada) and makeup (qada). Understanding their precise definitions and types is essential for analyzing how obligations are discharged in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish ada and qada
Recognize that ada is delivering the exact act as commanded, while qada delivers its equivalent when the original is impossible.
The key difference is the object delivered: the same act vs. its equivalent.
2
Identify the three types of ada
Categorize performance as complete pure, deficient pure, or resembling qada based on timing and conditions.
Complete: on time with all conditions. Deficient: on time but lacking some conditions. Resembling qada: performed after preferred time but within extended time.
3
Identify the three types of qada
Categorize makeup by rational equivalent (e.g., compensation), non-rational equivalent (e.g., prayer form), or in the sense of performance when time is still present.
Rational equivalent: can be measured, e.g., value of a lost item. Non-rational: acts of worship where exact form is prescribed.
4
Apply the usurpation example
Contrast returning a usurped item (ada) with compensating for its destruction (qada) to see the practical application.
If the item exists, returning it is ada; if lost, paying its value is qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب بيان صفة حكم الأمر وذلك نوعان : أداء، وقضاء. والأداء أنواع ثلاثةٌ: أداء كامل محض، وأداء قاصر محض، وما هو شبية بالقضاء. والقضاء أنواع ثلاثة : نوع بمثل معقول ونوع بمثل غير معقول، ونوع بمعنى الأداء. أيضاً. وهذه الأقسام تدخل في حقوق الله تعالى، وتدخل في حقوق العباد فالأداء : اسم لتسليم نفس الواجب بالأمر. والقضاء : اسم لتسليم مثل الواجب ،به كمن غصب شيئاً: لزمه تسليم الله عينه ، ورده فيصير به مؤدياً، وإذا هلك لزمه ضمانه، فيصير به قاضياً. وقد يدخل في الأداء قسم آخر، وهو النفل، على قول من جعل الأمر حقيقةً في الإباحة ،والندب فأما القضاء فلا يحتمل هذا الوصف. قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُكُمْ أَن تُؤَدُّوا الْأَمَنتِ إِلَى أَهْلِهَا ﴾ النساء /٥٨ ، وإنه في تسليم أعيانها إلى أربابها. وقد تدخل إحدى العبارتين في قسم العبارة الأخرى، فيُسمى الأداء قضاء؛ لأن القضاء لفظ متّسع. وقد يُستعمل الأداء في القضاء مقيَّداً؛ إلا أن للأداء خصوصاً بتسليم نفس الواجب وعينه ؛ لأن مرجع العبارة إلى الاستقصاء، وشدة الرعاية، كما قيل في الثلاثي منه : الذئب يأدو للغزال يأكله أي يحتال ويتكلف فيَختله. وأما القضاء : فإحكام الشيء نفسه لا ينبيء عن شدة الرعاية. : واختلف المشايخ رحمهم الله في القضاء أيجب بنص مقصود، أم بالسبب الذي يوجب الأداء؟ فقال بعضُهم : بنص مقصود ؛ لأن القُربة عُرفت قُربةً بوقتها، وإذا فاتت عن وقتها : فلا يعرف لها مثل إلا بالنص المقصود، وكيف يكون مثلاً لها بالقياس وقد ذهب وصف فضل الوقت؟ وقال عامتهم : يجب بذلك السبب. وبيان ذلك : أن الله تعالى أوجب القضاء في الصوم بالنص، فقال تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ ( البقرة / ١٨٤ . وجاءت السنة بالقضاء في الصلاة، قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام مَن نام عن صلاة أو نسيها : فليصلها إذا ذَكَرَها ، فإن ذلك وقتها »
Chapter on the description of the ruling of command. And that is of two types: performance (ada) and makeup (qada). And performance is of three types: complete pure performance, deficient pure performance, and what resembles makeup. And makeup is of three types: a type with a rational equivalent, a type with a non-rational equivalent, and a type in the sense of performance. Also. And these divisions enter into the rights of Allah Most High and enter into the rights of servants. So performance (ada) is a name for delivering the exact obligated act by the command. And makeup (qada) is a name for delivering the equivalent of the obligated act. For example, whoever usurps something: he is required to deliver its exact entity and return it, thereby becoming a performer (muaddiyan); and if it perishes, he is required to guarantee it, thereby becoming a make-upper (qadiyan). And another category enters into performance: supererogatory (nafl), according to the one who makes command (amr) literal in permissibility and recommendation. As for makeup, it does not admit this description. Allah Most High said: “Indeed, Allah commands you to render trusts to their owners” (al-Nisa 4:58). And it is about delivering their exact entities to their owners. And one of the two expressions may enter into the category of the other expression, so performance is called makeup, because makeup is a broad term. And performance may be used in the sense of makeup when restricted; however, performance has specificity in delivering the exact obligated act and its entity, because the reference of the expression is to thoroughness and intense care, as is said in its triliteral form: the wolf “ya'du” (approaches) the gazelle to eat it, i.e., it contrives and exerts effort to deceive it. As for makeup (qada): it is perfecting the thing itself, not indicating intense care. And the scholars differed—may Allah have mercy on them—regarding makeup: is it obligated by a specific text (nass maqsud) or by the cause that obligates performance? Some said: by a specific text, because the act of worship is known as worship by its time, and when it passes its time, its equivalent is not known except by a specific text, and how can there be an equivalent for it by analogy when the attribute of the virtue of the time has gone? And the majority of them said: it is obligated by that cause (the cause that obligates performance). And the explanation of that: Allah Most High obligated makeup in fasting by text, so He said: “then a number of other days” (al-Baqarah 2:184). And the Sunnah came with makeup in prayer: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: “Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time.”
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh opens the chapter on the characteristics of the ruling of command. The author begins by dividing the fulfillment of a command into two types: أداء (ada, performance) and قضاء (qada, makeup). Ada is further categorized into three types: complete pure performance (e.g., on time with full conditions), deficient pure performance (on time but lacking some conditions), and what resembles qada (e.g., performing an obligatory prayer after its preferred time but within its full time). Qada is also three types: a type that has a rational equivalent (like paying for a lost item), a type without a rational equivalent (like making up a missed prayer, which has no exact substitute in form), and a type that is similar to ada (when the time is still extended). These categories apply both to rights of Allah (like missed prayers) and rights of servants (like returning a borrowed item). The author then defines linguistically: ada is delivering the exact wajib (the very act), while qada is delivering its equivalent (like paying compensation for a destroyed item). The example of usurpation clarifies: if the item exists, returning it is ada; if it perished, paying its value is qada. Supererogatory acts are considered ada under a view that 'amr includes recommendation. Qada does not include supererogatory because it only applies to obligatory acts missed. The verse from Surah al-Nisa emphasizes returning exact things (ada). The author notes that sometimes ada is called qada loosely. Etymologically, ada implies thoroughness and care (like a wolf stalking prey), while qada simply means finishing something without that nuance. The passage concludes with a significant usul dispute: does the obligation of qada (making up a missed act) arise from a new specific text (nass) or from the same cause that made the original act obligatory? Some scholars argue that since the virtue of time is lost, only a new text can establish the obligation of an equivalent act. The majority however hold that the original cause (like the command to pray) still obligates qada, supported by the Quranic text for fasting and the hadith for prayer where the Prophet said 'that is its time' for the makeup. The Hanafi position follows the majority, taking the hadith as evidence that the same cause continues.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-ada'): Delivering the exact wajib act as commanded, on time or with full conditions.
القضاء (al-qada'): Delivering the equivalent of the wajib act when the original is missed or destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what is the definition of ada?
A) Delivering the equivalent of the wajib act.
B) Delivering the exact wajib act by the command.
C) Delivering a similar act at any time.
D) Delivering any act of worship.

Key Takeaway
Ada is delivering the exact wajib by command; qada is delivering its equivalent when the original is missed.

The Obligation of Qada: Specific Text or Original Cause?
Presents a dispute on whether qada is obligated by a new text or the original cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on the obligation of qada and evaluate the Hanafi majority argument using the proofs cited.

Core Idea
The Hanafi majority holds that qada is obligated by the same cause as ada, not by a new text.

After defining ada and qada, al-Bazdawi presents a key usul dispute: does the obligation to make up a missed act of worship arise from a new specific text (nass maqsud) or from the same cause (sabab) that obligated the original? Understanding this debate is crucial for deriving rulings on missed obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions: some scholars say qada requires a new text; the majority says it is obligated by the same cause.
The passage refers to 'some' (بعضهم) and 'the majority' (عامتهم).
2
Examine the opposing proof
Understand why some argue that worship is time-specific, so a new text is needed for makeup.
They argue that the virtue of time (fadl al-waqt) is lost, so analogy cannot establish an equivalent.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze the Quranic verse for fasting (al-Baqarah 2:184) and the hadith for prayer ('that is its time') as evidence that the same cause continues.
The verse implies qada is from the same obligation; the hadith explicitly says the makeup time is the time of the prayer.
4
Determine the practical difference
Consider a scenario where no explicit text exists for makeup: the Hanafi still obligates it; the opposing view does not.
For example, if a missed prayer had no specific text for its makeup, the opposing view would not consider it obligatory.

Complete Performance (Al-Ada' al-Kamil) in Huquq al-Ibad
Introducing the categories of rights of servants and defining complete performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define complete performance (al-ada' al-kamil) in the context of rights of servants and identify scenarios where it applies versus where it does not.

Core Idea
Complete adaa requires returning the exact object, not its value.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul introduces a fundamental distinction in Hanafi usul: the category of huquq al-ibad (rights of servants) and the precise meaning of complete performance. Understanding this definition is crucial for later rulings on liability, ghasb, and debt. The passage sets the stage for differentiating between fulfilling a right exactly and merely compensating.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the passage is discussing huquq al-ibad (rights of servants) as opposed to huquq Allah.
This classification affects whether the right can be waived or requires strict execution.
2
Note the example given
The passage mentions 'the debt' (al-dayn) as an illustration of how rights of servants are divided.
Debt is a common example of a right of a servant that must be fulfilled completely.
3
Define complete adaa
Complete performance is defined as returning the exact same right ('ayn al-haqq) in cases of ghasb and sale, and paying the debt in full.
The key is exactness: returning the identical item or the precise amount owed.
4
Contrast with incomplete adaa
Consider what happens when the exact item is destroyed or unavailable: the liability shifts to paying the value (qimah), which is not considered complete adaa.
This distinction has practical consequences for discharge of liability.
5
Understand the practical effect
Complete adaa discharges the liability exactly; if only compensation is given, the obligation may still be considered unfulfilled in a technical sense.
This affects later rulings on guarantee, daman, and the permissibility of substitute performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حقوق العباد فهي تنقسم على هذا الوجه. الدين. أما الأداء الكامل : فهو ردُّ عين الحق في الغصب والبيع وأداء الدين
As for the rights of servants, they are divided in this manner: the debt. As for complete performance (adaa), it is returning the exact same right in cases of usurpation (ghasb) and sale, and paying the debt.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the rights of human beings (huquq al-ibad). It states that these rights are divided into categories, and then gives an example: the debt. Then it defines complete adaa (performance) as returning the exact object of the right in cases of ghasb (usurpation) and sale, and paying the debt. This is a concise definition that will likely be expanded in subsequent pages. In Hanafi fiqh, complete adaa means fulfilling the obligation exactly as required, without any deficiency.

Key Terms
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): The rights that pertain to human beings, as opposed to rights of Allah.
الأداء الكامل (al-ada' al-kamil): Complete performance that fulfills the right exactly, by returning the same object or paying the debt.
عين الحق ('ayn al-haqq): The exact object of the right; the specific item that is owed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for complete adaa (al-ada' al-kamil) in cases of ghasb and sale?
A) Paying the market value of the item.
B) Returning the exact same right ('ayn al-haqq).
C) Offering an apology and compensation.
D) Returning a similar item of equal value.

Key Takeaway
Complete adaa for rights of servants requires returning the exact object owed, not a substitute.

Shubhah and the Ruling of Recitation in the Last Two Rak'ahs
Textual analysis of recitation in last two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi use of shubhah to derive the ruling that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is adā' in one respect, and evaluate the effect of this classification on the obligation of al-Fātiḥah and sūrah.

Core Idea
A doubt (shubhah) transforms qadā' into adā' in the last two rak'ahs, preventing the obligation from falling away entirely.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul examines a classic Hanafi example: the recitation in the last two rak'ahs of prayer. The author demonstrates how a solitary hadith (khabar al-wāhid) determines the first two rak'ahs, while a doubt (shubhah) about the last two being a locus for recitation leads to a nuanced ruling. Understanding this analysis sharpens your ability to apply usul principles like shubhah and adā'/qadā' to fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central usul problem
The author asks: Is recitation in the last two rak'ahs adā' (timely) or qadā' (make-up)? The classification affects whether omission requires make-up. Note that the entire prayer is a locus for recitation, but the first pair is specified by khabar al-wāhid.
The first pair's recitation is firmly established; the last pair's status is ambiguous.
2
Trace the role of khabar al-wāhid
The first pair (shaf‘ awwal) is definitively determined by a solitary report (khabar al-wāhid) that necessitates action. This leaves the second pair with only a doubt (shubhah) of being a locus for recitation.
Khabar al-wāhid provides zanni certainty but is sufficient for obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply the concept of shubhah
Because the second pair retains a doubt of being a locus for recitation, it is from one aspect not missed (fā'it). This doubt transforms the recitation into adā' in that aspect, even though in reality it is qadā'.
Shubhah prevents the act from being purely qadā', thus avoiding the need for a separate make-up.
4
Derive the fiqh consequences
If al-Fātiḥah is omitted in the last two, it falls away (tasquṭ) because it was prescribed only as a precaution (ihtiyāt). Treating it as adā' would lead to repetition. The sūrah is not obligatory as qadā' because the last two do not originally require a sūrah; its obligation arises only from considering adā'.
The ruling: no make-up for al-Fātiḥah; no obligation for sūrah at all in the last two.
5
Connect to the hadith evidence
The footnote cites hadiths from Ali, Ibn Mas‘ūd, Abū Qatāda, and Jābir showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited only al-Fātiḥah in the last two rak‘ahs. These hadiths serve as the khabar al-wāhid that specifies the first pair and leaves a shubhah for the second.
The hadiths confirm that the last two have a different recitation pattern, supporting the analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضع القراءة جملة الصلاة، إلا أن الشفع الأول تعين بخبر الواحد الذي يوجب العمل، وقد بقي للشفع الثاني شبهة كونه محلاً، وهو من هذا الوجه ليس بفائت، فوجب أداؤها؛ اعتباراً لهذه الشبهة وإن كان قضاءً في الحقيقة.
ولهذا لو ترك الفاتحة سقطت؛ لأن المشروع من الفاتحة في الأُخريين إنما شرع احتياطاً؛ فلم يستقم صرفها إلى ما عليه، ولم يستقم اعتبار معنى الأداء؛ لأنه مشروع أداء، فيتكرر الأداء، فلذلك قيل تسقط، والسورة لم تجب قضاء؛ لأنه ليس عنده في الأخريين قراءة سورة يصرفها إلى ما عليه، وإنما وجب لاعتبار الأداء.
(۱) قوله : إلا أن الشفعَ الأول تعيَّن بخبر الواحد قال الشارح: هو ما روي عن علي رضي الله عنه : «القراءة في الأوليين : قراءة في الأخريين». قلت : فيه تأمل. وأصرح منه ما روى ابن أبي شيبة عن علي وابن مسعود قالا: «اقرأ في الأُوليين، وسبِّح في الأُخريَيْن».
وعن أبي قتادة قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ في الظهر في الأُوليَيْن بأُمِّ الكتاب وسورتين، وفي الركعتين الأخريين بأُمِّ الكتاب، ويُسمعنا الآيةَ أحياناً». متفق عليه.
وعن جابر بن عبد الله رضي الله عنه قال: «سُنَّةُ القراءة في الصلاة: أن يقرأ في الأُوليين بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة ، وفي الأُخريين بأم القرآن». رواه الطبراني في الوسط.
The place of recitation is the entire prayer, except that the first pair (of rak'ahs) is determined by a solitary report (khabar al-wāhid) which necessitates action, and for the second pair there remains the doubt (shubhah) of it being a locus (for recitation), and from this aspect it is not missed, so its performance (adā') is obligatory, considering this doubt, even though it is in reality a make-up (qadā'). For this reason, if one omits al-Fātiḥah, it falls away; because the prescribed al-Fātiḥah in the last two (rak'ahs) is prescribed only as a precaution; so it is not proper to divert it to its (original) requirement, and it is not proper to consider the meaning of adā' because it is prescribed as adā', then adā' would be repeated, therefore it is said it falls away. And the sūrah is not obligatory as qadā' because according to him there is no recitation of a sūrah in the last two to divert to its requirement; rather it is obligatory only due to considering adā'. (Then the footnote text quotes hadiths.)
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the ruling on recitation in the last two rak'ahs of prayer. The author begins by stating that recitation is prescribed for the entire prayer, but the first two rak'ahs are specifically determined by a solitary hadith (khabar al-wāhid), while the last two retain a doubt (shubhah) as a locus for recitation. Because of this doubt, the recitation in the last two is considered adā' (timely performance) in one sense, even though in reality it is qadā' (make-up) since the original time for recitation was the first two. This subtlety leads to the ruling that if one omits al-Fātiḥah in the last two, it is not made up later (it falls away) because it was prescribed as a precaution (ihtiyāt) and treating it as adā' would lead to repetition. The sūrah (additional chapter) is also not made up because the last two do not originally require a sūrah; its obligation is only due to considering adā'. The footnote provides supporting hadiths from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Abu Qatada, and Jabir that confirm recitation in the last two is with al-Fātiḥah alone, supporting the idea that it is a different kind of obligation.

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): Timely performance of an act of worship within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qadā'): Make-up performance of an act of worship after its time has passed.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that affects the legal classification of an act.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāhid): A solitary hadith narrated by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawātur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a person omits al-Fātiḥah in the last two rak'ahs of a prayer?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) He must perform sajdat al-sahw.
C) The recitation of al-Fātiḥah falls away (tasquṭ) and is not made up.
D) He must recite it after the prayer as qadā'.

Key Takeaway
The shubhah surrounding the last two rak'ahs prevents the recitation from being pure qadā', so the obligation of al-Fātiḥah is precautionary and falls away if omitted.

Complete and Deficient Performance (Adā') in the Rights of People
Classifies adā' into complete and deficient with examples and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish complete from deficient performance (adā') in rights of people, and apply the Hanafi rulings to cases involving defective delivery, base coins, and substitution of mahr.

Core Idea
A right is fully discharged only when both essence (ʿayn) and description (waṣf) are fulfilled; deficiency in description makes performance incomplete.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, how a right is fulfilled matters as much as what is fulfilled. This passage classifies performance (adā') in the rights of people into complete (kāmil) and deficient (qāṣir) using concrete examples from property law. The classification reveals a nuanced approach where the 'same object' may be returned, but defects or changes in description can affect whether the obligation is truly discharged. We will explore the examples of a slave returned with a liability, payment with base coins, and a mahr that changes form, noting the internal ikhtilāf among the Madhhab founders.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two fundamental categories of adā'
The text defines complete performance as returning the exact same object (ʿayn) in ghaṣb or sale without any defect. Deficient performance is delivering the essence but with a defect in description (waṣf).
Focus on the distinction between aṣl (essence, genus, or identity) and waṣf (description, quality, or attribute).
2
Analyze the slave case: returning a slave with a liability
If a usurper returns a slave who is now 'busy' (mashghūl) with a jināyah or debt, does that constitute complete delivery? Abu Hanifa says no—it is like a claim of ownership (istiḥqāq) and delivery is nullified if the slave perishes. The two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) say yes—a defect does not prevent complete delivery; it is just a defect and the owner can seek compensation.
Note the thamarah al-khilāf: if the slave perishes, Abū Ḥanīfa voids the original right; the two uphold delivery and allow recourse for the defect.
3
Examine the base coins (zuyūf) example
Paying a debt with base coins without the creditor's knowledge is deficient because the genus (aṣl) matches but the description (waṣf) is lacking (coins are not sound). Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad rule that if the coins perish, the creditor's right is totally void (essence taken, description gone with no equivalent). Abū Yūsuf uses istiḥsān to oblige the debtor to pay an equivalent of the defective portion.
Here istiḥsān overrides strict qiyās to preserve the creditor's right in the description.
4
Understand the mahr case: performance in the sense of qadā'
When a man marries a woman with her father (who is his slave) as mahr, and the father is later claimed (istiḥqāq), the husband owes the value. If he later acquires ownership before paying, he must hand the father over to the woman. This is 'performance in the sense of qadā'' because the change of ownership turns the obligation into delivering the very same object, but considered as an equivalent.
This shows that even when the object changes status, the right to the same 'ayn may persist in a transformed manner.
5
Synthesize the criteria for complete vs. deficient adā'
Complete adā' requires delivery of the exact same object without any defect in essence or description. Deficient adā' occurs when the essence is correct but the description is flawed. The ruling on whether the obligation is discharged depends on the nature of the defect and the possibility of compensation.
This classification is a key usul tool for analyzing rights of people (huqūq al-ʿibād) in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حقوق العباد فهي تنقسم على هذا الوجه.
الدين.
أما الأداء الكامل : فهو ردُّ عين الحق في الغصب والبيع وأداء (۱)
والقاصر مثل أن يغصب عبداً فارغاً ثم يرده مشغولاً بالجناية أو الدين، أو يسلم المبيع مشغولاً بالجناية أو الدين، أو ما أشبه ذلك، حتى إذا هلك في ذلك الوجه : انتقض التسليم عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه ؛ لأنه بمنزلة الاستحقاق.
وعندهما هذا تسليم كامل ؛ لأن العيب لا يمنع تمام التسليم، وهو عيب عندهما، وأداء الزيوف في الدين إذا لم يعلم به صاحب الحق: أداء بأصله ؛ لأنه من جنس حقه، ولكن ليس بأداء بوصفه لعدمه، فصار قاصراً. ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة ومحمد رضي الله عنهما : إنها إذا هلكت عند القابض بطل حقه أصلاً؛ لأنه لما كان أداءً بأصله: صار مستوفياً، وبطل الوصف؛ لأنه لا مثلَ له لا صورةً ولا معنى، ولم يجز إبطال الأصل للوصف، إذ الإنسان لا يضمن لنفسه.
واستحسن أبو يوسف، وأوجب مثل المقبوض؛ إحياء لحقه في هذا الوصف.

والأداء الذي هو في معنى القضاء، مثل أن يتزوج رجل امرأة على أبيها، وهو عبده، فاستحق: وجبت قيمته.
فإن لم يُقض بقيمته حتى مَلَكَ الزوج الأب بوجه من الوجوه : لزمه تسليمه إلى المرأة ؛ لأنه عين حقها.
في العين
إلا أنه في معنى القضاء؛ لأن تبدل الملك : أوجب تبدلاً حكماً، فكان هذا عين حقها في المسمى، لكن بمعنى المثل. ولهذا قلنا : إن الزوج إذا مَلَكَه : لا يملك أن يمنعها إياه؛ لأنه حقها.
عين
As for the rights of people, they are divided in this way: The debt. As for complete performance (adā' kāmil), it is returning the very same right (‘ayn al-ḥaqq) in cases of usurpation (ghaṣb) and sale, and performance (marked with footnote 1). Deficient performance is like when someone usurps a free slave and then returns him busy with a criminal liability (jināyah) or debt, or delivers the sold item busy with jināyah or debt, or similar. So if it perishes in that condition, the delivery is nullified according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) because it is like a claim of ownership (istiḥqāq). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this is complete delivery because a defect does not prevent complete delivery, and it is a defect according to them. And the payment of base coins (zuyūf) in a debt, if the claimant is unaware, is performance in its essence (aṣl) because it is from the same genus as his right, but it is not performance in its description (wasf) due to its absence, so it becomes deficient. For this reason, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: If they perish with the recipient, his right is totally void; because when it was performance in its essence, he becomes recipient of the right, and the description is void because there is no equivalent (mithl) for it, neither in form nor meaning, and it is not permissible to invalidate the essence for the description, since a person does not guarantee for himself. Abu Yusuf practiced istiḥsān and obligated the equivalent of what was received, to revive his right in this description. And performance that is in the sense of qadā' is like when a man marries a woman with the mahr being her father, who is his slave, and then the father is claimed (istiḥqāq): the value (value) becomes due. If the value is not paid until the husband acquires ownership of the father by some means, he is obliged to hand him over to the woman because he is the very same right of hers. However, it is in the sense of qadā' because the change of ownership necessitated a change in legal rule, so this is the very same right of hers in the named (mahr), but in the sense of an equivalent (mithl). For this reason we say: If the husband acquires him, he does not have the right to prevent her from him, because he is her very own right.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a classification of types of performance (adā') in the rights of people (huqūq al-'ibād). The author begins by stating that these rights are divided similarly to the earlier discussion. 'Complete performance' (adā' kāmil) is returning the exact same object ('ayn) in cases of ghaṣb (usurpation) and sale. Deficient performance (adā' qāṣir) is illustrated by returning a slave who was originally free but now has a liability (jināyah or debt) attached. Abu Hanifa holds that if the slave perishes in this condition, the delivery is invalidated because it is as if the object is claimed (istiḥqāq). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is complete delivery because a defect does not prevent the fulfillment of delivery; the defect is considered a mere deficiency. Another example: paying a debt with base coins (zuyūf) without the creditor's knowledge. This is performance in essence (aṣl) because the coins are from the same genus as the debt, but not in description (wasf) because they are defective. Hence it is deficient. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that if the coins perish with the recipient, the creditor's right is completely void: the essence is received (the debt is paid), and the description (quality) is lost without an equivalent, so the essence is not invalidated for a non-existent equivalent. Abu Yusuf, using istiḥsān (juristic preference), argues that the debtor must pay an equivalent of the defective portion to preserve the creditor's right. The passage then gives an example of 'performance in the sense of qadā':' a marriage mahr where the husband pays a slave (the wife's father) who is later claimed by a third party. The husband owes the value, but if he comes to own the slave before paying, he must give the slave to the wife as the very same object, but it is considered qadā' because the change of ownership alters the legal status. This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach to defining proper fulfillment of rights.

Key Terms
أداء كامل (adā' kāmil): Complete performance: returning the exact same object (ʿayn) in ghaṣb or sale without defect.
أداء قاصر (adā' qāṣir): Deficient performance: delivering the essence but with a defect in description, e.g., base coins or a slave with a liability.
زيوف (zuyūf): Base coins (counterfeit or deficient in metal content) used as payment.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A claim of ownership that invalidates a prior transaction or delivery.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; Abu Yusuf uses it to obligate an equivalent for the defective portion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Hanifa when a usurper returns a slave who is now busy with a debt (mashghūl bi-dīn) and the slave then perishes?
A) The delivery is valid and the owner can claim the debt from the usurper.
B) The delivery is invalidated (intiqāḍ al-taslīm), so the usurper's original liability remains.
C) The owner must accept the slave and pursue the debtor.
D) The usurper is free from liability because he returned the slave.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a right may be fulfilled in its essence but deficient in description; the ruling on discharge depends on whether the defect is treated as a mere compensable liability or a fundamental obstacle to performance.

Deficient Performance (al-Adā' al-Qāṣir): Definition and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Definition of deficient performance with examples and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of deficient performance, apply it to examples, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on its effect when the object perishes.

Core Idea
Deficient performance is valid in essence but flawed in description; destruction may nullify the right or require compensation.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul introduces the concept of deficient performance (al-adā' al-qāṣir), a key Hanafi usul category. It clarifies that some acts of delivery or payment are valid in their basic substance but deficient in an attribute, and the ruling when the object perishes differs among the Hanafi masters. Understanding this distinction is crucial for deriving rulings in contracts and debts.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition
Identify the two components of deficient performance: it is valid in essence (aṣl) but deficient in description (waṣf). Note the examples: returning a slave with an encumbrance or paying with deficient coins.
The deficiency is in the attribute, not the substance.
2
Analyze the slave example
Consider the case: a free slave is usurped and returned with a crime or debt attached. According to Abu Hanifa, if the slave perishes, the delivery is reversed (like istihqāq). His two disciples consider it complete delivery; the defect does not prevent validity.
This shows how the same facts can be classified differently based on the view of deficiency.
3
Examine the deficient coin example
Payment with deficient coins (al-ziyūf) when the creditor is unaware: it is a payment in essence (same genus) but not in description (counterfeit). If the coins perish, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the debt is void; Abu Yusuf says the debtor must pay the equivalent.
The dispute hinges on whether the description can be compensated independently.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reason that the essence of the right has been received, and the description has no equivalent (lā mithla lahu), so it cannot be revived. Abu Yusuf uses istiḥsān to preserve the creditor's right in the description.
The difference is methodological: adherence to qiyas vs. istihsan.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: if deficient coins perish, the creditor loses the right under the majority view, but under Abu Yusuf, he can claim an equivalent.
This affects real transactions involving counterfeit currency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقاصر مثل أن يغصب عبداً فارغاً ثم يرده مشغولاً بالجناية أو الدين، أو يسلم المبيع مشغولاً بالجناية أو الدين، أو ما أشبه ذلك، حتى إذا هلك في ذلك الوجه : انتقض التسليم عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه ؛ لأنه بمنزلة الاستحقاق. وعندهما هذا تسليم كامل ؛ لأن العيب لا يمنع تمام التسليم، وهو عيب عندهما، وأداء الزيوف في الدين إذا لم يعلم به صاحب الحق: أداء بأصله ؛ لأنه من جنس حقه، ولكن ليس بأداء بوصفه لعدمه، فصار قاصراً. ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة ومحمد رضي الله عنهما : إنها إذا هلكت عند القابض بطل حقه أصلاً؛ لأنه لما كان أداءً بأصله: صار مستوفياً، وبطل الوصف؛ لأنه لا مثلَ له لا صورةً ولا معنى، ولم يجز إبطال الأصل للوصف، إذ الإنسان لا يضمن لنفسه. واستحسن أبو يوسف، وأوجب مثل المقبوض؛ إحياء لحقه في هذا الوصف.
The deficient (performance) is like when someone usurps a free slave and then returns it occupied with a crime or debt, or delivers the sold item occupied with a crime or debt, or something similar. So if it perishes in that state, the delivery is nullified according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, because it is like the case of rescindment. But according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this is a complete delivery, because a defect does not prevent complete delivery, and it is a defect in their view. And paying with deficient coins in a debt, if the right-holder is unaware of it, is a payment in essence because it is of the same genus as his right, but it is not a payment in description due to its deficiency, so it becomes deficient. Therefore, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: If they (the coins) perish with the recipient, his right is nullified entirely because when it was a payment in essence, he became a receiver, and the description is void because there is no equivalent for it in form or meaning, and it is not permissible to void the essence for the description, since a person does not guarantee for himself. Abu Yusuf opted for istihsan and required the equivalent of what was received, to revive his right in this description.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses deficient performance (al-adā' al-qāṣir). The author first gives examples: usurping a slave that is free (fārigḥ) and then returning it with a defect (e.g., a crime or debt attached); or delivering a sold item with such encumbrances. According to Abu Hanifa, if the item perishes in this state, the delivery is reversed, resembling the case of rescission (istihqāq). However, his two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) consider it a complete delivery because a defect does not prevent the delivery from being considered complete; it merely constitutes a defect (ʿayb). The second example is paying a debt with counterfeit or defective coins (al-ziyūf) when the creditor is unaware. Such payment is considered a payment in terms of the principal (aṣl) because it is of the same genus, but not in description (waṣf) due to deficiency, so it is deficient. If these coins perish in the creditor's possession, Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad rule that the creditor's right is completely nullified because he has effectively received the principal (aṣl) of his right, and the description is lost, having no equivalent in form or meaning. Thus, the principal cannot be invalidated for the sake of the description. Abū Yūsuf, however, uses istiḥsān and obligates the debtor to pay an equivalent (mithl) to revive the creditor's right in the description.

Key Terms
القاصر (al-qāṣir): Performance that is valid in essence but deficient in description due to a defect or deficiency.
الاستحقاق (al-istihqāq): Rescission of a contract due to a claim by a third party.
أداء الزيوف (adā' al-ziyūf): Payment with counterfeit or substandard coins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, when Abu Hanifa says the delivery of a returned slave is nullified if the slave perishes, he compares it to which concept?
A) Istihsan
B) Istihqāq (rescission)
C) Qiyas
D) Ijma

Key Takeaway
Deficient performance is valid in essence but deficient in description; when the object perishes, the Hanafi school's majority holds the right is void, while Abu Yusuf uses istihsan to require compensation.

Performance in the Sense of Compensation (al-Adā' fī Ma'nā al-Qaḍā')
Explaining marriage case where mahr is a slave then reclaimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining features of al-adā' fī ma'nā al-qaḍā' and apply the derived rulings to analogous cases in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A reacquired specified mahr is delivered as an equivalent, not a mere return.

This lesson unpacks a subtle category of legal performance where a specific object functions as compensation. Using the classic example of a slave given as dower and later reclaimed, you will learn how ownership changes affect obligations. Understanding this concept sharpens your ability to classify actions under hukm al-adā'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage and note the initial situation: a man marries a woman with her father (his slave) as mahr, then the father is reclaimed by a third party.
The slave is the 'ayn of the mahr.
2
Analyze the Legal Problem
When the father is reclaimed, the husband owes the value (qīma). But before that value is adjudicated, the husband reacquires the father. Determine how this changes the obligation.
Key: timing of reacquisition matters.
3
Extract the Ruling
The husband must now deliver the father himself, not pay value. This is because the father is the very substance (ʿayn) of her right, but due to the ownership interruption, it functions as an equivalent (mithl).
This is performance 'in the sense of compensation'.
4
Apply the Derived Furū'
Work through the sub-rulings: after reacquisition, the husband cannot withhold; the wife does not own until delivery; freeing or selling by the husband is valid but he owes value.
Each ruling follows from the object's dual nature.
5
Formulate the Definition
Based on the case, define 'performance in the sense of compensation': delivery of a specific object that, due to a change in ownership, counts as compensatory rather than pure delivery.
Compare with pure qaḍā' (payment of value) and pure adā' (delivery of the same ʿayn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأداء الذي هو في معنى القضاء، مثل أن يتزوج رجل امرأة على أبيها، وهو عبده، فاستحق: وجبت قيمته. فإن لم يُقض بقيمته حتى مَلَكَ الزوج الأب بوجه من الوجوه : لزمه تسليمه إلى المرأة ؛ لأنه عين حقها. إلا أنه في معنى القضاء؛ لأن تبدل الملك : أوجب تبدلاً حكماً، فكان هذا عين حقها في المسمى، لكن بمعنى المثل. ولهذا قلنا : إن الزوج إذا مَلَكَه : لا يملك أن يمنعها إياه؛ لأنه عين حقها. ولهذا قلنا: إنه لا يعتق عليها قبل القبض حتى يسلمه إليها، أو يُقضى به لها ؛ لأنه مثل من وجه، فلا تملك إلا بالتسليم. ولهذا قلنا : إذا أعتقه الزوج، أو كاتبه أو باعه قبل التسليم: صح؛ لأنه مثل من وجه، وعليه قيمته. إن حقها لا يعود إليه. ولهذا قلنا : إن كان القاضي قضى بقيمته على الزوج، ثم ملكه الزوج : من غير ( وهذه الجملة في نكاح الجامع الكبير مذكورة. )
And the performance that is in the sense of compensation is like a man marrying a woman with her father as dowry, while the father is his slave, then (the father) is claimed (by a third party): his value becomes due. And if his value is not adjudicated until the husband comes to own the father by any means, he is obliged to deliver him to the wife, because it is the very substance of her right. However, it is in the sense of compensation because the change of ownership necessitated a change in effect, so this is the very substance of her right in the named (dowry), but in the sense of an equivalent. Therefore we said: When the husband owns him, he cannot withhold him from her, because it is the very substance of her right. Therefore we said: He (the father) does not become free (from the wife) before delivery until he (the husband) delivers him to her, or it is adjudicated for her; because it is an equivalent in one sense, so she does not own except by delivery. Therefore we said: If the husband frees him, or makes a kitaba agreement, or sells him before delivery, it is valid, because it is an equivalent in one sense, and the husband owes his value. Her right does not return to him. Therefore we said: If the judge adjudicated his value upon the husband, then the husband owns him, (the situation...) This summary is mentioned in the Nikah chapter of al-Jami' al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage defines a type of performance that is considered compensation (al-adā' fī ma'nā al-qaḍā'). The example: a man marries a woman, and the dower (mahr) is set as the woman's father, who is a slave owned by the husband. If the father is later claimed by a third party (mustahaqq) and declared not the husband's property, the husband must pay the father's value as the mahr. However, if the husband later acquires ownership of the father by any means (purchase, gift, etc.) before the value is adjudicated, he is required to deliver the father himself to the wife. This is because the father is the exact object of her right (ʿayn ḥaqqihā). Despite being a specific object, it is considered as compensation because the change in ownership effectively transformed it into an equivalent (mithl). The author derives several rulings: (1) Once the husband owns the father, he cannot withhold him from the wife. (2) The wife does not own the father until he is delivered to her or adjudicated in her favor, because it is an equivalent in one aspect. (3) If the husband frees, makes a kitaba (contract of manumission), or sells the father before delivery, these acts are valid, and the husband owes the value (qīma) to the wife—her right does not revert. The passage references the detailed discussion in the 'Marriage' section of al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr.

Key Terms
في معنى القضاء (fī ma'nā al-qaḍā'): Performance that functions as compensation or discharge of a liability, rather than a simple delivery.
عين الحق (ʿayn al-ḥaqq): The very substance or specific object of a right, as opposed to its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the marriage example, if the husband frees the father (the mahr) before delivering him to the wife, what is the ruling?
A) The freeing is invalid and the husband must deliver the father.
B) The freeing is valid and the husband owes the value to the wife.
C) The wife automatically owns the father.
D) The marriage is annulled.

Key Takeaway
Performance in the sense of compensation (al-adā' fī ma'nā al-qaḍā') applies when a specified object is reclaimed and then reacquired before adjudication, requiring delivery as an equivalent.

Dispute on Feeding Usurped Food: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Deception (Ghurur)
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on performance with deception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ghurur in performance and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Reaching the substance suffices; ignorance does not void performance.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of performance when an owner feeds usurped food to the usurper without informing him. At stake is whether deception (ghurur) invalidates an otherwise complete act of delivery. By parsing the arguments, you will learn how each school prioritizes different legal principles and how the practical effect differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the contested ruling
Read the passage and note the exact scenario: a usurper takes food, then the owner feeds it to the usurper without telling him it is his own property. The dispute is whether this counts as valid performance that discharges the usurper's liability.
Focus on the act of feeding by the owner, not the initial usurpation.
2
Extract the Shafi'i position and its basis
Al-Shafi'i argues the performance is not commanded because it involves deception; people do not guard against their own property in permissible contexts, and the Law did not command deception. Therefore, the performance is void.
The key term is 'ghurur' (deception).
3
Extract the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafis counter that the performance is real because the very substance (ʿayn) of the owner's property reached the usurper's hand. Even if deficient, destruction would perfect it; ignorance does not invalidate the obligation. Custom that contradicts religion is null.
Hanafi emphasis on physical delivery over intentionality.
4
Parse the refutation of the Shafi'i argument
The Hanafi response addresses the 'defect' claimed by Shafi'i: it arose from ignorance, but ignorance does not invalidate; it is disgraceful, not an excuse to alter the obligatory duty.
Notice the rhetorical force: 'ignorance is disgraceful enough, how could it be an excuse?'
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi law, the usurper is discharged and no longer liable; under Shafi'i law, the usurper remains liable and must compensate the owner because the performance was invalid.
This difference has real-world implications for claims and restitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتصل بهذه الجملة : أن مَن غصب طعاماً، فأطعمه المالك أن يُعلِمَه : لم يبرأ عند الشافعي رحمه الله ؛ لأنه ليس بأداء مأمور به؛ لأنه غُرور، إذ المرء لا يتحامى في العادات عن مال غيره في موضع الإباحة، والشرع لم يأمر بالغُرور، فبطل الأداء ؛ نفياً للغرور، فصار معنى الأداء لغواً؛ رداً للغرور. وقلنا نحن هذا أداء حقيقةً ؛ لأن عَيْنَ ماله وَصَلَ إلى يده، ولو كان قاصراً لتم بالهلاك، فكيف لا يتم وهو في الأصل كامل؟ وأما الخلل الذي ادعاه، فإنما وقع لجهله والجهل لا يُبطله، وكفى بالجهل عارا، فكيف يكون عذرا في تبديل إقامة الفرض اللازم. والعادة المخالفة للديانة الصحيحة على ما زعم: لغو؛ لأن عين ماله وصل إلى يده.
Connected to this topic: Someone who usurps food, and the owner feeds it to him without informing him (that it is his own food) – according to al-Shafi'i, he is not discharged, because it is not a commanded performance, due to deception. One does not guard against the property of others in customary permissibility, and the Law did not command deception, so the performance is void to negate deception, rendering the meaning of performance null and void. We (Hanafis) say: This is real performance, because the very substance of his property reached his hand. Even if it were deficient, it would be completed by destruction, so how could it not be complete while it is originally complete? As for the defect he claims, it arose from ignorance, and ignorance does not invalidate it. Ignorance is disgraceful enough, how could it be an excuse to alter the fulfilment of the obligatory duty? And custom that contradicts sound religion, as he claims, is null and void, because his property reached his hand.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding a scenario: a person usurps food, and the owner later feeds that same food to the usurper without informing him that it is his own (usurped) property. The question is whether this counts as valid performance (adā') that discharges the usurper's liability. Al-Shafi'i argues that it is not valid because the owner is not commanded to feed the usurper in this manner; it involves deception (ghurūr), as people do not normally guard against using their own property when it is made permissible. Since the Law does not command deception, the performance is void. The Hanafis counter that this is genuine performance because the very substance (ʿayn) of the owner's property reaches the usurper's hand. Even if it were a deficient performance (qāṣir), it would be perfected upon destruction (as earlier rule). Here, the performance is originally complete (kāmil). The defect that al-Shafi'i claims arises from the owner's ignorance, but ignorance does not invalidate the ruling; rather, it is a disgrace. Therefore, the usurper is discharged. The Hanafis also dismiss any contrary custom as irrelevant.

Key Terms
الغرور (al-ghurūr): Deception, i.e., causing someone to mistakenly think they are consuming their own property when it is actually the owner's.
أداء حقيقة (adā' ḥaqīqa): Performance that is valid in reality as per the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the usurper discharged when the owner feeds him the usurped food without informing him?
A) Because the owner intended to forgive the debt.
B) Because the very substance of the owner's property reached the usurper's hand.
C) Because the usurper had a right to eat the food.
D) Because the Shafi'i argument is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis hold that physical delivery of the ʿayn constitutes valid adāʾ, even if the owner acts deceptively, because ignorance does not invalidate the obligation.

Compensation by Rational Equivalent: Complete Type
Defining complete compensation by equivalent in form and meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'complete compensation by rational equivalent' and identify its role as the default principle in Hanafi tort law (ḍamān al-ʿudwān).

Core Idea
Complete compensation is the default in Hanafi tort law: return the same item in form and meaning.

This passage introduces a key classification in Hanafi damages: whether compensation should be by an equivalent (mithl) or by value. The author defines the complete type—which matches both form and meaning—and states that it is the default principle in guarantees arising from wrongful aggression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of compensation
The text states that compensation by a rationally conceivable equivalent (al-qaḍā' bi mithl maʿqūl) is divided into two types: complete (kāmil) and deficient (qāṣir).
Focus on the complete type for this lesson.
2
Define the complete type
The complete type is defined as 'the equivalent in form and meaning' (al-mithl ṣūratan wa maʿnan). This means the compensation must match the original item both in its physical attributes (form) and its purpose or function (meaning).
Form (ṣūra) refers to outward characteristics; meaning (maʿnā) refers to the intended use or value.
3
Recognize its legal position
The complete type is described as 'the original (aṣl) in the guarantee of aggression (ḍamān al-ʿudwān).' This means it is the default rule when compensation is due for a wrongful act.
This contrasts with compensation by value (qīma), which applies when mithl is not possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القضاء بمثل معقول، فنوعان كامل، وقاصر. أما الكامل : فالمثل صورةً ومعنى، وهو الأصل في ضمان العدوان،
As for compensation by a rationally conceivable equivalent, it is of two types: complete and deficient. As for the complete: it is the equivalent in form and meaning, and it is the original in the guarantee of aggression.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This short passage introduces a division of compensation (qaḍā') by a rationally ascertainable equivalent (mithl maʿqūl). It explains that this compensation can be complete (kāmil) or deficient (qāṣir). The complete compensation is the mithl that matches both in form (ṣūra) and meaning (maʿnā), and it serves as the default principle (aṣl) in guarantees arising from wrongful aggression (ḍamān al-ʿudwān). This sets the stage for further discussion on the deficient type, which is cut off in this window.

Key Terms
المثل المعقول (al-mithl al-maʿqūl): An equivalent that can be rationally determined, having both form and meaning.
ضمان العدوان (ḍamān al-ʿudwān): Guarantee arising from wrongful aggression (tort).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the 'original' (aṣl) in the guarantee of aggression (ḍamān al-ʿudwān)?
A) The equivalent in form and meaning.
B) The monetary value of the object.
C) The deficient type of compensation.
D) The judgment of the ruler.

Key Takeaway
Complete compensation by rational equivalent (mithl kāmil) is the default in Hanafi tort law, requiring the equivalent in form and meaning.

Valuation of Usufruct in Hanafi Usul
Establishes that usufruct lacks valuation and contracts are based on substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling that usufruct (manafi') is not subject to valuation (taqawwum) by analyzing Quranic verses and consensus, and explain why contracts for usufruct remain valid.

Core Idea
Usufruct cannot be valued because it cannot be preserved, yet contracts for it are valid by substitution.

This passage tackles a key usul question: why is usufruct (manafi') not considered valued property (mal mutaqawwim) despite being the subject of valid contracts like hire (ijarah)? The author, likely al-Bazdawi, provides a clear istinbat from Quranic texts and consensus, showing that valuation requires the possibility of preservation (ihraz), which usufruct lacks. The legitimacy of such contracts arises from the principle of substitution (khilafah), where the substance stands in for the benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage asks: why is usufruct not subject to valuation in contracts? Recognize that valuation (taqawwum) is a legal attribute requiring the property to be capable of preservation (ihraz).
2
Analyze the first Quranic verse (an-Nisa 24)
The verse 'that you seek with your wealth' (أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ) is used to show that marriage requires valued property, which is acquired through preservation. This establishes the link between valuation and preservation.
The operative phrase is 'with your wealth' (بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ), indicating that the wealth must be mutaqawwim.
3
Analyze the second Quranic verse (al-Qasas 27)
The verse 'and that you hire me' (وَعَلَى أَنْ تَأْجُرَنِي) deals with a hire contract (usufruct). It does not mention valuation, implying that usufruct is not valued.
The absence of any qualification regarding the property being valued supports the conclusion.
4
Apply the principle of consensus (ijma)
The author states that the permissibility of contracts for usufruct is established by consensus, overriding any analogical reasoning (qiyas) that would require valuation.
Consensus here is a stronger evidence than qiyas, which would otherwise demand valuation.
5
Derive the final ruling
Thus, usufruct lacks taqawwum, but contracts for usufruct are valid based on substitution (khilafah) of the substance. The ruling: usufruct is not mal mutaqawwim, yet its contracts are sahih by ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يجب التمييز بين الجائز والفاسد؛ لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى الحرج، فلم يُعتبر فيما شُرع ضرورة. والمنافع إذا وجدت لم تحتمل البقاء للإحراز، فلا تثبت لها صفة التقوم بحال. وأما جواز العقد فبناءً على قيام العين مقام المنفعة بطريق الخلافة؛ قضاء للحوائج، وذلك أمر مشروع عند الحاجة بالإجماع. ولا يلزم أنها تقومت في باب العقود، وليس إلى التقوم حاجة، إذ الاستبدال صحيح من غير التقوم؛ لأن ذلك ثابت بالإجماع، بخلاف القياس عند التراضي بما قلنا إن التقوم من غير إحراز غير معقول. وإنما قلنا ذلك؛ لأن الله تعالى شرع ابتغاء الأبضاع بشرط المال المتقوم، حيث قال: ﴿أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ﴾ [النساء/24]، وإنما يُضاف إلينا بواسطة الإحراز. وشرع الابتغاء بالمنافع لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى أَنْ تَأْجُرَنِي﴾ [القصص/27]. وبطلت المقايسة؛ لأن للرضا أثراً في إيجاب الأصول والفضول جميعاً.
And it is not obligatory to distinguish between valid and invalid [contracts] because that leads to hardship, so it is not considered in what is legislated out of necessity. And usufructs, when they exist, cannot endure for preservation, so the attribute of valuation (taqawwum) is not established for them in any case. As for the permissibility of the contract, it is based on the substance standing in place of the usufruct by the way of succession (khilafah) to fulfill needs, and that is a thing legislated when necessary by consensus. And it does not necessarily follow that they become valued in the chapter of contracts, and there is no need for valuation, because substitution is valid without valuation; because that is established by consensus, unlike analogy when there is mutual consent, because we said that valuation without preservation is unintelligible. We only said that because Allah the Exalted legislated seeking marriage with the condition of valued property, where He said: 'that you seek with your wealth' [an-Nisa 24], and it is only attributed to us by means of preservation. And He legislated seeking with usufruct by His saying: 'and that you hire me' [al-Qasas 27]. And the analogy is invalid because consent has an effect in establishing obligations and optional matters alike.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof regarding the nature of usufruct (manafi') in contracts. It begins by stating that there is no need to distinguish between valid and invalid contracts because that would cause hardship; necessity overrides. Then it explains that usufructs, unlike physical objects, cannot be preserved (ihraz), so they do not have the attribute of valuation (taqawwum). Despite that, contracts for usufruct (like hire) are permissible because the substance (ayn) stands as a substitute for the usufruct by way of succession (khilafah) to meet needs. This is established by consensus (ijma). The author then clarifies that this does not mean usufructs become valued in contracts; substitution (istibdal) is valid without valuation. He cites Quranic verses: marriage requires valued property (mal mutaqawwim) because it is acquired through preservation (ihraz), while hire (usufruct) is based on the verse about hiring for wages. Finally, he invalidates analogical reasoning (muqayasah) that would require valuation because consent (rida) has an effect in both obligatory and voluntary matters.

Key Terms
تقوم (taqawwum): The attribute of being valued property that can be preserved (ihraz).
منافع (manafi'): Usufructs, benefits that cannot be preserved physically.
خلافة (khilafah): Succession; the substance standing in place of the usufruct in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are contracts for usufruct (like hire) valid despite usufruct not being subject to valuation (taqawwum)?
A) Because usufruct is actually valued by scholars.
B) Because the substance (ayn) stands as a substitute for the usufruct by way of succession.
C) Because usufruct becomes valued through preservation.
D) Because valuation is not required for any contract.

Key Takeaway
Usufruct (manafi') is not subject to valuation (taqawwum) because it cannot be preserved; however, contracts for usufruct are valid by consensus based on substitution (khilafah) of the substance.

Marital Authority Is Not a Guaranteed Property: A Hanafi Usul Principle
Argument that marital right is not a guaranteed property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that milk al-nikah is not mal mutaqawwim to determine liability in cases of false testimony and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position using qiyas.

Core Idea
Marital authority is not property—false testimony after consummation incurs no liability.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul presents a core Hanafi usul principle: milk al-nikah (the right of marital authority) is not a guaranteed financial property (mal mutaqawwim). The author defends this by analogy and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view. Understanding this principle is crucial for determining liability in cases involving marriage rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the opening claim: 'إن ملك النكاح لا يُضمن' (marital authority is not guaranteed). This is the Hanafi stance.
The principle is that milk al-nikah is not mal mutaqawwim.
2
Examine the Reasoning
The author lists characteristics: milk al-nikah can be annulled without witnesses/guardian, does not involve seizure (istila'), and is a release (itlaq). These show it is not financial property.
Contrast with mal mutaqawwim which is subject to seizure and compensation.
3
Apply to Post-Consummation False Testimony
Since milk al-nikah is not mal mutaqawwim, a witness who falsely testifies to divorce after consummation is not liable for compensation. The passage states this explicitly.
No liability because nothing of financial value was lost.
4
Distinguish Pre-Consummation Case
For false testimony before consummation, the witness must pay half the named dower. This is not a value for the sexual organ (bud'), but a restriction on the husband's property resembling usurpation (ghasp).
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi rationale.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i Position
Al-Shafi'i would hold that full comparable dower is due when the sexual organ is lost, implying it is valuable. The Hanafi response is that the named dower is not a value for bud'; half is only a restriction showing it is not full compensation.
The thamarah al-khilaf: different rulings on liability for false testimony after consummation.

It is recommended, so it is permissible to disregard it, rather it is good. For this we say: indeed the ownership of marriage is not guaranteed by testifying to divorce after consummation, nor by killing the wife or her apostasy; because it is not a valuable property; rather the sexual organ is valued with money out of veneration for its importance. Importance is for the owned object; as for the right over it, no. Thus it is valid to annul it without witnesses or guardian. For this reason it is not given the ruling of being valuable upon termination, because it does not involve seizure, rather it is a release. And we are not bound by testimony of divorce before consummation, for when retracted it necessitates guarantee of half the dower; because that is not a value for the sexual organ. Do you not see that the full comparable dower is not obligated, as al-Shafi'i said, but the named dower obligated by contract is not entitled to be delivered upon the lapse of delivery of the sexual organ. So when they obligate him to deliver half despite the loss of delivery of the sexual organ, it is a restriction of his hand over that property, resembling usurpation. As for the judicial award that is in the ruling of performance, like a man who marries a woman for a slave not specified: if he pays its value, she is forced to accept; and the value of a thing is a discharge (qada') for it inevitably, and it is resorted to only when unable to deliver the original. Since the original is unknown in one respect and known in another, its delivery is valid in one respect and incapacity is possible; if he delivers it is valid, and if he chooses the side of incapacity to deliver the original, its value becomes due. And since the original cannot be realized in delivery except by specification, and specification is only by valuation, valuation becomes an original in this respect, so the value competes with the named. Unlike a specific slave; because it is known without valuation, so its value is pure discharge and is not considered when capable. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a legal argument concerning the nature of marital authority (milk al-nikah). The author argues that the right over a wife is not a guaranteed property (mal mutaqawwim). Therefore, if someone gives false testimony that a woman is divorced after consummation, or kills the wife, or she apostatizes, the witness is not liable for the value of the marriage right, because it is not financial property. The sexual organ (bud') is valued only in dowry out of reverence, but the right itself (milk) is not. The ruling is that marital authority can be invalidated without witnesses or guardian. When marriage ends, there is no liability for loss of this right because it is a release, not seizure. The author distinguishes the case of testifying to divorce before consummation: if retracted, the witness must pay half the dower, but that is not value for the sexual organ; it is a restriction on the husband's property resembling usurpation. Then he discusses a marriage for a non-specified slave: if the husband pays the value, the wife must accept. The original (the slave) is uncertain in one way, certain in another, so value is a legitimate substitute. Unlike a specific slave, whose value is only a discharge when the original can be delivered.

Key Terms
ملك النكاح (milk al-nikah): The right of marital authority, the legal relationship between spouses established by marriage.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is valuable and subject to legal trade and compensation.
قضاء (qada'): A substitute discharge fulfilling an obligation when the original is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The witness must pay half the named dower.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that marital authority is not a guaranteed property is proven by its characteristics: it can be annulled without formalities and is a release, not a seizure; this determines liability in cases involving marriage.

The Goodness of a Command is Known by Being Commanded
Principle that command's goodness is known by being commanded, not by reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the goodness of a command is known only by the Lawgiver's command and explain why reason alone does not determine legal goodness.

Core Idea
Goodness in law is a revealed attribute, not a rational one.

In this brief but foundational passage, al-Bazdawi sets down the Hanafi position on the source of moral-legal goodness (husn). The statement is axiomatic: a command is good because Allah commanded it, not because human reason deems it so. This separates the Hanafi school from those who hold that reason can independently determine value. As a memorization anchor, this principle underpins much of Hanafi usul, especially in debates about obligation before revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of the ruling
Locate the term 'hukm al-amr' (the ruling of the command). Understand that this is the legal attribute attached to a command itself, not the action commanded.
The 'command' here is the shari' command (al-amr al-shar'i).
2
Extract the core claim
The text says the ruling of a command is 'described as good' (موصوف بالحسن). That goodness is known 'by its being commanded' (بكونه مأموراً به), not by reason.
This is a direct refutation of rationalist ethics.
3
Understand the negation
The phrase 'لا بالعقل نفسه' (not by reason itself) emphasizes that reason on its own cannot establish legal goodness or obligation.
Hanafis do not deny that reason can perceive benefit, but it cannot create law.
4
Grasp the ontological status of reason
The text states 'العقل غير موجب بحال' (reason is not a cause in any case). Reason does not generate obligation; only the Lawgiver does.
This is a key difference from the Mutakallimin.
5
Recognize the chapter purpose
The closing 'this chapter is for its division' signals that this principle is the basis for classifying types of commands (e.g., fard, wajib, sunnah).
Understanding this axiom is necessary for later distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و
ومن قضية الشرع في هذا الباب أن حكم الأمر موصوف بالحسن،
و
عُرف ذلك بكونه مأموراً ،به لا بالعقل نفسه، إذ العقل غير موجب بحال،
،
وهذا الباب لتقسيمه، والله الموفق
And from the decree of the law in this chapter is that the ruling of a command is described as good, and that is known by its being commanded, not by reason itself, for reason is not a cause in any case. And this chapter is for its division. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage states a foundational usul principle: the legal ruling of a command (hukm al-amr) is characterized as good (hasan), and this goodness is known because it has been commanded by the Lawgiver, not because reason independently judges it to be good. Reason does not impose obligation on its own; all obligation comes from revelation. The phrase 'this chapter is for its division' indicates that this is the introduction to a section classifying types of commands.

Key Terms
الحسن (al-hasan): A legal attribute meaning 'good', applied to actions commanded by the Lawgiver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) By its being commanded by the Lawgiver.
C) By consensus of scholars.
D) By analogy to other good acts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the goodness of a command is a revealed attribute, not a rational one; reason cannot impose legal obligation.

Classification of Goodness in Commanded Acts
Classifying types of goodness in commanded acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any commanded act according to Al-Bazdawi's taxonomy of goodness (husn), distinguishing intrinsic from instrumental goodness and identifying the appropriate subtype.

Core Idea
The goodness of an act is defined by the command, not reason, and is divided into six types across two categories.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh presents the Hanafi view that the goodness (husn) of a commanded act is known solely from the fact that it is commanded by the Lawgiver, not from rational judgment. The author then provides a detailed sixfold classification of commanded acts based on whether their goodness is intrinsic or instrumental. This taxonomy is a key tool for analyzing the legal and moral status of actions in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Establish the epistemological premise
Note that Al-Bazdawi emphasizes that husn is known from the command, not reason. Reason has no obligating force.
This is a key Hanafi principle distinguishing from Mutakallimin.
2
Divide into two primary categories
Separate acts that are good for a meaning in themselves (hasan li-dhatih) from those good for a meaning in another (hasan li-ghayrih).
These are the two fundamental divisions.
3
Analyze the three subtypes of intrinsic goodness
Identify which type never loses its goodness (e.g., faith), which can lose it, and which resembles instrumental.
Only one subtype is absolutely permanent.
4
Analyze the three subtypes of instrumental goodness
Identify the types based on how the purpose is attained: self-standing, by the act itself, or conditional.
The third subtype is called 'comprehensive'.
5
Apply the taxonomy to an example
Use the example of faith (iman) as the first type of intrinsic goodness that never loses its descriptor.
Faith is always good by itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قضية الشرع في هذا الباب أن حكم الأمر موصوف بالحسن، وعرف ذلك بكونه مأموراً به لا بالعقل نفسه، إذ العقل غير موجب بحال. وهذا الباب لتقسيمه، والله الموفق. باب بيان صفة الحسن للمأمور به المأمور به نوعان في هذا الباب: حسن لمعنى في نفسه، وحسن لمعنى في غيره. فالحسن لمعنى في نفسه ثلاثة أضرب: ١ - ضرب لا يقبل سقوط هذا الوصف بحال. ٢ - وضرب يقبله. ٣ - وضرب منه ملحق بهذا القسم، لكنه مشابه لما هو حسن لمعنى في غيره. والذي هو حسن لمعنى في غيره ثلاثة أضرب أيضاً: ١ - فضرب منه: ما هو حسن لمعنى في غيره، وذلك الغير قائم بنفسه مقصوداً، لا يتأدى بالذي قبله بحال. ٢ - وضرب منه: ما هو حسن لمعنى في غيره، لكنه يتأدى بنفس المأمور به فكان شبيهاً بالذي حسن لمعنى في نفسه. ٣ - وضرب منه ما هو حسن لحسن في شرطه بعد ما كان حسناً لمعنى في نفسه، أو ملحقاً به، وهذا القسم يُسمى جامعاً. وأما الضرب الأول من القسم الأول: فنحو الإيمان بالله تعالى،
And from the ruling of the Law in this chapter is that the ruling of the command is described as good, and that is known by it being commanded, not by reason itself, for reason is not obligatory in any case. And this chapter is for its division, and Allah is the Grantor of success. Chapter: Explanation of the attribute of goodness for the commanded act. The commanded act in this chapter is of two types: good for a meaning in itself, and good for a meaning in other than itself. The good for a meaning in itself is of three types: 1 - A type that does not accept the removal of this description in any case. 2 - And a type that accepts it. 3 - And a type from it attached to this division, but it is similar to what is good for a meaning in other than itself. And what is good for a meaning in other than itself is also of three types: 1 - A type from it: what is good for a meaning in other than itself, and that other is self-subsisting and intended, not attained by the preceding at all. 2 - And a type from it: what is good for a meaning in other than itself, but it is attained by the commanded act itself, so it becomes similar to what is good for a meaning in itself. 3 - And a type from it: what is good for goodness in its condition after it was good for a meaning in itself or attached to it, and this division is called comprehensive. As for the first type of the first division: such as faith in Allah Almighty,
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bazdawi's usul introduces the classification of the 'goodness' (husn) of commanded acts (al-mamur bih). The author first establishes that the goodness of a commanded act is known from the fact that it is commanded by Allah, not from rational judgment alone, because reason has no inherent obligating force. Then he opens a new chapter on the attribute of goodness. The commanded act is divided into two primary categories: (1) good for a meaning in itself, i.e., intrinsically good, and (2) good for a meaning in other than itself, i.e., instrumentally good. Each category has three sub-types. Intrinsic goodness has: a type that never loses this description (like faith in Allah); a type that can lose it (like certain acts of worship that may become invalid); and a type attached to this division but resembling instrumental goodness (e.g., acts that are good in themselves but also serve another purpose). Instrumental goodness also has three: a type where the other purpose is self-standing and not attained by the act alone; a type where the act itself attains the purpose, resembling intrinsic goodness; and a type that becomes good due to a condition in its own goodness (called 'comprehensive'). This taxonomy helps scholars analyze the moral and legal value of actions.

Key Terms
حسن (ḥusn): Goodness or praiseworthiness of an act from a legal perspective.
مأمور به (ma'mūr bih): The act that is commanded by Allah, subject to evaluation of its goodness.
معنى في نفسه (maʻnan fī nafsih): A meaning or attribute inherent to the act itself, making it intrinsically good.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Acts that are good for another purpose
B) Acts that never lose the description of goodness
C) Acts that can lose the description of goodness
D) Acts that are similar to instrumental goodness

Key Takeaway
Al-Bazdawi's sixfold taxonomy of commanded acts is a foundational tool for Hanafi usul, linking the goodness of an act directly to the command of the Lawgiver.
