The Condition of Nisab: Initiation vs Continuation of Zakah Obligation
Explains that nisab is a condition for initiating zakah obligation but not for its continuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that nisab is a condition only for the initiation of zakah obligation, not its continuation, and apply it to scenarios of partial loss or consumption of nisab, distinguishing it from the condition of growth.

Core Idea
Nisab triggers zakah; once triggered, the obligation persists proportionally even if nisab falls below the threshold.

The obligation of zakah arises when a person owns wealth reaching the nisab threshold. But what happens if that wealth later decreases? Does the obligation vanish or remain? This passage from al-Bazdawi’s Usul al-Fiqh clarifies that nisab is a condition for the initiation of the obligation, not for its continuation. The reasoning draws on the nature of the duty and the concept of capacity (ghina), and distinguishes it from other conditions like growth (nama').

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
State the Hanafi position: nisab is a condition for initiating zakah obligation but not for its continuation. If nisab decreases after obligation, zakah remains on the remaining wealth proportionally.
This is the main proposition the passage defends.
2
Understand the Counter-Argument and Its Refutation
Examine the hypothetical objection: if nisab were required for continuation, the duty would become pure compensation (gharamah), changing its nature. The passage rejects this because the ratio (1/40) stays constant regardless of the base.
The ratio is key: paying 5 from 200 or 1 from 40 is the same fraction.
3
Analyze the Rationale: Ghina as a Description (Wasf)
The condition of nisab is rooted in the need for the person to be wealthy (ghina) to be capable of giving. Since 'abundance' has no fixed limit, the Law set a specific number (nisab). This condition applies only at the start.
Ghina is an added capacity beyond being a simple owner.
4
Distinguish from the Condition of Growth (Nama')
The property's potential for growth facilitates payment; this condition must persist. If the asset loses growth potential, the obligation changes. This contrasts with the nisab condition.
Growth (nama') is a condition of the obligation's continuation because it affects the nature of the duty.
5
Apply to Cases of Consumption and Destruction
If the owner consumes (wastes) the nisab, the obligation does not fall; it becomes a debt (ghurm) because the nisab was a right of the poor. The consumer is a transgressor.
This is an exception: consumption does not extinguish the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التيسير، فلو قلنا ببقاء الواجب بدون النصاب : لانقلب غرامةً محضة، فيتبدل الواجب، فلذلك سقط بهلاك المال.
ولا يلزم أن النصاب شرط لابتداء الوجوب، ولا يشترط لبقائه، فإن كل جزء من الباقي يبقى بقسطه ؛ لأن شرط النصاب لا يُغيّر صفةَ الواجب. ألا يُرى أن تيسير أداء الخمسة من المئتين وتيسير أداء الدرهم من الأربعين سواء، لا يختلف؛ لأنه ربع عشر بكل حال.
لكن الغنى وصفٌ لا بدَّ منه ليصير الموصوف به أهلاً للإغناء، إذ الإغناء من غير الغني لا يتحقق، كالتمليك من غير المالك، والغنى بكثرة المال، وليس للكثرة حد تُعرف به، وأحوال الناس فيه شتى، فقدر الشرع بحد واحد، فصار ذلك شرطاً للوجوب لما كان أمراً زائداً على الأهلية الأصلية.
وشَرْطُ الوجوب: لا يُشترط دوامه، إذ الوجوب في واجب واحد لا يتكرر، فأما قيام المال بصفة النماء فميسر للأداء ، فتغير به صفة الواجب، فشَرَطنا دوامه.
وهذا بخلاف استهلاك النصاب، فإنه لا يُسقط الحق، وقد صار غُرْماً؛ لأن النصاب صار في حق الواجب حقاً لصاحب الحق، فيصير المستهلك متعدياً على صاحب الحق ، فعد قائماً في حق صاحب الحق، فصار الواجب على هذا التقدير غير متبدل.
The facilitation, for if we say that the duty remains without the nisab: it would turn into a pure compensation, thus the duty changes, therefore it falls due to destruction of wealth. It does not follow that nisab is a condition for the initiation of obligation and not required for its continuation, for every part of the remaining [wealth] remains with its share; because the condition of nisab does not change the nature of the duty. Do you not see that the facilitation of paying five from two hundred and the facilitation of paying one dirham from forty are the same, not different; because it is one-fourth of a tenth in every case. But wealth is a description that is necessary for the described person to become capable of giving, for giving from one who is not wealthy is not realized, like ownership from one who does not own. Wealth is abundance of property, and abundance has no known limit, and people's circumstances vary, so the Law fixed a single limit, so that became a condition for obligation since it is something additional to the original capacity. And the condition of obligation: its continuity is not required, since obligation in a single duty is not repeated. As for the property being in a state of growth, it facilitates payment, so it changes the nature of the duty, so we required its continuity. This is contrary to the consumption of the nisab, for it does not annul the right, and it becomes a debt; because the nisab becomes a right of the right-holder regarding the duty, so the consumer becomes a transgressor against the right-holder, thus it is considered as remaining with respect to the right-holder, so the duty on this estimation is not changed.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the condition of nisab in the obligation of zakah. It begins by rejecting the idea that nisab must persist throughout the period of obligation, arguing that if it did, the duty would become a mere compensation (gharamah) and change nature. Instead, nisab is only a condition for the initiation of obligation; once established, the obligation continues even if the nisab is partially lost, because each part of the remaining wealth carries its share of the duty proportionally. The author explains that the ratio (one-fourth of a tenth) remains constant whether paying five dirhams from two hundred or one dirham from forty. The deeper reason is that wealthiness (ghina) is a description required for the capacity to give, and since this description lacks a natural limit, the Law fixed a specific quantitative limit (nisab) as a condition for obligation. This condition is only for the initial obligation; it does not require continuity because a single obligation is not repeated. However, the property's potential for growth (nama') facilitates payment, so that quality must persist. Finally, if the nisab is consumed (destroyed) by the owner, it does not cancel the right; instead, it becomes a debt (ghurm) because the nisab was a right of the poor. The consumer is considered a transgressor, so the obligation remains unchanged.

Key Terms
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that must exist for the obligation to arise, but not necessarily to continue once the obligation is established.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams for silver) that triggers the obligation of zakah.
الغنى (al-ghina): Wealth that meets the nisab threshold, making one capable of giving zakah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the obligation of zakah if the nisab is partially lost after the obligation has begun?
A) The obligation is completely cancelled.
B) The obligation remains on the remaining wealth proportionally.
C) The obligation becomes a debt (ghurm).
D) The obligation changes to a different type of duty.

Key Takeaway
Nisab is a condition for the initiation of zakah obligation, not its continuation; once the obligation is established, it persists proportionally even if nisab decreases.

Effect of Debt on Capacity for Kaffara vs Zakat
Usul rule on qudra and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi usul principle regarding capacity (qudra) in the presence of debt and distinguish its application to the obligations of kaffara and zakat.

Core Idea
Debt removes the condition of ease for zakat but not for kaffara; present inability suffices for fasting.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh clarifies a key legal nuance: how debt affects a person's capacity to perform financial obligations. The Lawgiver's choice between wealth and fasting in expiations hinges on present inability, not lifelong inability. The same reasoning does not apply to zakat, which requires surplus wealth (ease). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying usul al-fiqh principles to obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
State the central question: how does debt affect the capacity to perform kaffara (expiation) vs zakat?
The text begins with a proof that capacity with wealth gives a choice, but when debt negates ease, the obligation may transfer.
2
Extract the Quranic evidence and its interpretation
Find the verse (5:89) and note that 'lam yajid' is interpreted as present inability, not lifetime inability.
The verse does not require assessing inability over a lifetime, only at the time of performance.
3
Apply the distinction between kaffara and zakat
Observe that zakat requires the attribute of ease (yusr) and the purpose of enrichment (ighna'), so debt removes ease; kaffara does not condition ease, only present inability.
The text explicitly contrasts the two: zakat is invalidated by debt, but kaffara is not.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute among later scholars
Recognize that some mashayikh hold fasting suffices because debt negates ease, while others require wealth-based expiation because kaffara differs from zakat.
The text presents both opinions without final tarjih, leaving it as a point of ikhtilaf.
5
Conclude with the underlying usul principle
Sum up: the effect of debt on a financial obligation depends on whether the obligation conditions ease and enrichment, or merely present capacity.
This principle is grounded in the nature of the obligation and the textual proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل عليه أن الشرع خيَّره عند قيام القدرة بالمال، والتخيير تيسير، ولأنه نُقِلَ إلى الصوم؛ لقيام العجز عند أداء الصوم مع توهم القدرة فيما يُستقبل.
ولم يُعتبر ما يُعتبر في عدم سائر الأفعال، وهو العدم في العمر كله، لكنه اعتبر العدم الحالي.
ألا يُرى أن الله تعالى قال: ﴿فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ﴾ (المائدة/89)، وتقدير العجز بالعمر يُبطل أداء الصوم، فعلم أنه أراد به العجز الحالي. وكذلك في طعام الظهار، وسائر الكفارات، فثبت أن القدرة ميسرة من قبيل الزكاة، إلا أن المال ها هنا غيرُ عين، فأي مال أصابه من بعد: دامت به القدرة. ولهذا ساوى الاستهلاك الهلاك ها هنا؛ لأن الحق لما كان مطلقاً الوقت، ولم يكن المال متعيّناً لم يكن الاستهلاك تعدياً، وصارت هذه القدرة على هذا التقدير نظير استطاعة الفعل التي لا تسبق الفعل.
ولهذا قلنا: بطل وجوب الزكاة بالدين؛ لأنه ينافي الغنى واليسر.
ولا يلزم أن الدين لا يمنع وجوب الكفارة، وهو ينافي اليسر؛ لأنه قال في كتاب الأيمان: رجلٌ له ألف درهم، وعليه دين أكثر من ألف درهم، فكفر بالصوم بعد ما قضى دينه بماله، قال: يجزئه.
ولم يذكر أنه إذا لم يصرف إلى دينه ما جوابه؟
فقال بعض مشايخنا يجزئه التكفير بالصوم؛ لما قلنا من فوات صفة اليسر به، فيُجعل المالُ كالمعدوم.
وقال بعضهم: بل تجب بالمال ولا يجزئه الصوم، بخلاف الزكاة. والفرق أن الزكاة وجبت بصفة اليسر، وشَرْط القدرة، ولمعنى الإغناء بقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "أغنوهم عن المسألة في مثل هذا اليوم". وبقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا صدقة إلا عن ظهر غنى". وهذا الإغناء وجب عبادةً؛ شكراً لنعمة الغنى، فشرط الكمال في سببه؛ ليُستحق شكره، فيكون الواجب شطراً من الكامل، والدين يُسقط الكمال، ولا يُعدِمُ أصله.
ولهذا حَلَّت له الصدقة، فلم يجب عليه الإغناء.
ولهذا لا تتأدى الزكاة إلا بعين متقومة.
The proof for it is that the Lawgiver gave him a choice when capacity exists with wealth, and choice is facilitation. And because he is transferred to fasting due to the existence of inability at the time of performing fasting while assuming capacity in what is future. And what is considered in the non-existence of other actions—which is non-existence throughout life—is not considered here; rather, present non-existence is considered. Do you not see that Allah the Exalted said: 'And whoever does not find (the means), then a fast of three days' (Al-Ma'idah 5:89), and estimating inability over a lifetime would nullify the performance of fasting, so it is known that He meant present inability. Similarly, in the food for zihar and all other expiations. Thus it is established that capacity is eased like in the case of zakat, except that the wealth here is not a specific item. So whatever wealth he obtains later, capacity continues with it. For this reason, consumption (by him) is equated with destruction here, because since the right is not tied to a specific time and the wealth is not specific, consumption is not transgression. And this capacity on this estimation becomes analogous to the capacity for an action that does not precede the action. For this reason we said: The obligation of zakat is invalidated by debt because it contradicts wealth and ease. But it does not follow that debt prevents the obligation of expiation while it contradicts ease, because he said in Kitab al-Ayman: A man who has one thousand dirhams and owes a debt of more than one thousand dirhams, then he performed expiation by fasting after paying his debt with his wealth—he said: It suffices him. And he did not mention what the answer is if he did not spend it on his debt. So some of our mashayikh said: Expiation by fasting suffices him due to what we said about the loss of the attribute of ease through it, so the wealth is treated as non-existent. And some of them said: Rather, expiation with wealth is obligatory and fasting does not suffice him, unlike zakat. The difference is that zakat became obligatory with the attribute of ease and the condition of capacity, and for the meaning of enrichment due to the Prophet's saying: 'Enrich them so they do not beg on a day like this.' And his saying: 'No charity except from surplus wealth.' And this enrichment is obligatory as worship, as thanks for the blessing of wealth, so perfection in its cause is required so that His thanks is deserved. Thus the obligatory is a portion of the perfect, and debt removes perfection but does not annihilate its origin. For this reason, charity became permissible for him, so enrichment is not obligatory upon him. For this reason, zakat is only fulfilled with a specific valuable item.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage discusses a crucial usul al-fiqh issue: the concept of capacity (qudra) and its interaction with debt (dayn) in obligations like kaffara and zakat. The text begins by establishing that the Lawgiver gives a choice when capacity with wealth exists, and that choice is a facilitation. When a person cannot pay with wealth, he is transferred to fasting, but this transfer is based on present inability, not lifelong inability. The Quranic verse (5:89) supports this by not requiring a lifetime assessment. Capacity here is 'eased' (yusr), similar to zakat, but with a difference: the wealth for expiation is not a specific asset (ghayr 'ayn), so any wealth obtained later sustains capacity. Thus, consumption (istihlak) by the owner is not tantamount to transgression. The text then applies this: zakat obligation is nullified by debt because it contradicts the condition of wealth (ghina) and ease (yusr). However, debt does not prevent obligation of kaffara, even though it negates ease. A man with debt more than his wealth can expiate by fasting after paying his debt—this suffices. There is a dispute among later scholars (mashayikh): some say fasting suffices because debt removes ease, treating wealth as non-existent; others say wealth-based expiation is obligatory because kaffara differs from zakat. The difference (farq) is that zakat is obligated on the basis of wealth and ease, and its purpose is enrichment (ighna') of the poor, which is a worship and thanks for wealth. Hence, perfection in the cause (wealth) is required. Debt removes perfection (kamal) but not the origin (asl). Therefore, a person in debt can receive charity (sadaqa) and is not obliged to give it; similarly, zakat requires a specific valuable asset ('ayn mutaqawwima) to be fulfilled. The passage essentially clarifies the legal principle that the effect of debt on obligations depends on the nature of the obligation: zakat requires ease as a condition, whereas kaffara does not.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): The legal capacity to perform an obligation, often tied to possession of means (mal) or ability.
اليُسر (al-yusr): Ease or surplus wealth beyond basic needs and debts, required for zakat.
الدين (al-dayn): Debt that a person owes, which may affect the attribute of wealth (ghina) and ease (yusr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does debt nullify the obligation of zakat but not of kaffara?
A) Because kaffara is more important than zakat.
B) Because zakat requires the condition of ease and enrichment, which debt removes, while kaffara only requires present inability.
C) Because debt is always forgiven in kaffara.
D) Because the Prophet exempted debtors from kaffara.

Key Takeaway
The effect of debt on capacity varies by obligation: it negates ease for zakat but not for kaffara, where present inability suffices.

Condition of Ease (Yusr) for Continuation of Obligations
Comparing conditions for obligation continuation across different duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qudra and yusr to determine whether an obligation continues after its initial conditions are lost, and derive analogous rulings using qiyas.

Core Idea
Some obligations continue only as long as ease (yusr) remains; others are satisfied by mere ability (qudra).

This passage is a foundational usul al-fiqh discussion from al-Bazdawi. It establishes that certain obligations, like expiation and tithe, require not only ability but also ease for their continuation. By contrast, Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr are conditioned only on ability. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct condition to obligations and for deriving new rulings through analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between two types of conditions for the continuation of obligations: qudra alone vs. qudra plus yusr.
This is a classification of the attribute of the command (sifat al-hukm).
2
Examine the base case: kaffara
Kaffara requires only ability and ease, not complete wealth. The author argues this because kaffara is not for enrichment but for concealment or deterrence.
Notice that the purpose of the obligation (maqsad) influences the conditions.
3
Apply qiyas to ushr and kharaj
By analogy (qiyas), ushr and kharaj also require ease. The loss of the crop (subject matter) removes ease, so the obligation falls.
The illa (effective cause) is the condition of ease in the obligation.
4
Contrast with Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr
Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr are conditioned only on ability. Once the obligation is established, loss of the means does not nullify it.
For Hajj, ease (servants, mounts) is not a condition by consensus.
5
Consider the effect of debt
Debt affects obligations differently depending on whether the condition is ability or ease. For kaffara, debt does not negate ease. For sadaqat al-fitr, debt negates the wealth condition. For zakat al-tijara, debt on the trade item negates the complete wealth required.
This shows how the rule applies consistently across different cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكفارة فلا تستغني عن شرط القدرة وعن قيام صفة اليسر في تلك القدرة، إلا أنها لم تُشرع للإغناء، ألا يُرى أنها شرعت ساترةً، أو زاجرة، لا أمراً أصلياً للفقير إغناء له. وألا يُرى أنه تتأدى بالتحرير وبالصوم ولا إغناء فيهما، لكن المقصود به نيل الثواب؛ ليقابل بموجب الجناية. وما تقع به كفاية الفقير في باب الكفارة يصلح سبباً للثواب، ولذلك تتأدى بالإباحة، ولا إغناء يحصل بها. فإذا لم يكن الإغناء مقصوداً: لم تُشترط صفة الغنى في المخاطب بها، بل القدرة واليُسر بها شرط، وذلك لا ينعدم بالدين، ويتبين أنها لم تجب شكراً للغنى، بل جزاءً للفعل، فلم يُشترط كمال صفة الغنى، وإنما شرط أدنى ما يصلح لكسب الثواب، وأصل المال كاف لذلك. وعلى هذا الأصل: يُخرَّج سقوط العُشر بهلاك الخارج؛ لأنه وجب بشرط القدرة الميسرة؛ لأن القدرة على أداء العُشر تستغني عن قيام تسعة الأعشار، لكنه شُرط ذلك؛ لليسر، ولم يجب إلا بأرض نامية بالخارج، فشرط قيامه لبقاء صفة اليُسر. وكذلك الخراج يسقط إذا اصطلم الزرعَ آفة؛ لأنه إنما وجب بصفة ألا يُرى أنه لا يجب إلا بسلامة الخارج، إلا أنه بطريق التقدير بالتمكن؛ لكون الواجب من غير جنس الخارج وبدليل أن الخارج إذا قل: حُطّ الخراجُ إلى نصف الخارج، ولما كان كذلك: سقط بهلاك الخارج، حتى لا ينقلب غُرماً محضاً. وهذا مخالف للحج، فإنه إذا وجب بملك الزاد والراحلة: لم يسقط بفَوْتهما؛ لأنه وجب بشرط القدرة، دون اليُسر، ألا يُرى أن الزاد والراحلة أدنى ما يُقطع به السفر، ولا يقع اليسر إلا بخَدَم ومراكب وأعوان، وليس بشرط بالإجماع، فلذلك لم يكن شرطاً لدوام الواجب. وكذلك لا تسقط صدقة الفطر بهلاك الرأس، وذهاب الغنى؛ لأنها لم تجب بصفة اليسر، بل بشرط القدرة، وقيام صفة الأهلية بالغنى، ألا يُرى أنها وجبت بسبب رأس الحر، ولا يقع به الغنى، ووجبت بالغنى بثياب البذلة والمهنة، ولا يقع بها اليسر؛ لأنها ليست بنامية، فلم يكن البقاء مفتقراً إلى دوام شرط الوجوب. ولا يلزم أنها لا تجب عند قيام الدين وقت الوجوب؛ لأن الدين يُعدِم الغنى الذي هو شرط الوجوب، وبه تقع أهلية الإغناء. بخلاف الدين على العبد، فإنه لا يمنع؛ لأنه لا يمنع قيام الغنى بمال آخر يفضل عن حاجته بالغاً مائتي درهم. بخلاف زكاة التجارة، فإنها تسقط بدين العبد الذي هو للتجارة؛ لأن الزكاة تقتضي صفة الغنى الكامل بعين النصاب، لا بغيره، والله أعلم. هذا الذي ذكرنا هو تقسيم في صفة حكم الأمر، وصفة المأمور به في نفسه فأما ما يكون صفةً قائمةً بغيره، وهو الوقت: فلا بد من ترتيبه على الدرجة الأولى. ***** وهذا باب تقسيم المأمور به في حكم الوقت:
As for expiation (kaffara), it is not independent of the condition of ability and the existence of the attribute of ease in that ability, except that it was not legislated for enrichment. Do you not see that it was legislated as a concealer or a deterrent, not as an original command to enrich the poor. And do you not see that it is discharged by freeing a slave and by fasting, and there is no enrichment in them, but the intended purpose is attainment of reward to correspond to the consequence of the offense. And that which suffices the poor in the matter of expiation is suitable as a means for reward, and therefore it is discharged by giving permission (ibaha), and no enrichment occurs thereby. So when enrichment is not intended, the attribute of wealth is not required in the addressee, rather ability and ease are the condition, and that is not negated by debt. And it becomes clear that it is not obligatory as gratitude for wealth, but as a recompense for the act, so completeness of the attribute of wealth is not required; rather the minimum that suffices for earning reward is required, and having capital itself is sufficient for that. And upon this principle is derived the falling of the tithe (ushr) due to destruction of the crop, because it became obligatory with the condition of ability accompanied by ease; because ability to pay the tithe is independent of the existence of nine-tenths, but that was conditioned for ease. And it was not obligatory except with land that produces a crop, so its existence was conditioned for the continuation of the attribute of ease. Similarly, the land tax (kharaj) falls if a pestilence destroys the crop, because it was obligatory only with the attribute [of ease] – do you not see that it is obligatory only with safety of the crop, except that it is by way of estimation based on capability, because the duty is not of the same genus as the crop, and by evidence that if the crop is little, the kharaj is reduced to half of the crop. And since that is the case, it falls with destruction of the crop, so that it does not turn into pure loss. This is contrary to Hajj, for if it becomes obligatory by ownership of provisions and mount, it does not fall by their loss, because it became obligatory with the condition of ability, not ease. Do you not see that the provisions and mount are the minimum to undertake the journey, and ease is not achieved except with servants, mounts, and helpers, and that is not a condition by consensus. Therefore, it is not a condition for the continuance of the obligation. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr (alms for breaking the fast) does not fall by destruction of the head [i.e., the person] or loss of wealth, because it was not obligatory with the attribute of ease, but with the condition of ability and existence of the attribute of eligibility through wealth. Do you not see that it became obligatory due to the head of a free person, and no [complete] wealth occurs thereby, and it became obligatory due to wealth in the form of ordinary and work clothes, and ease does not occur thereby because they are not productive. So continuance was not dependent on the continuance of the condition of obligation. And it does not follow that it is not obligatory when debt exists at the time of obligation, because debt negates the wealth that is the condition of obligation, and through it eligibility for enrichment occurs. Contrary to the debt upon a slave, for it does not prevent [obligation], because it does not prevent the existence of wealth from another property that exceeds his need, reaching two hundred dirhams. Contrary to zakat on trade (zakat al-tijara), for it falls by the debt of the slave that is for trade, because zakat requires the attribute of complete wealth in the very nisab, not in other than it. And Allah knows best. This that we have mentioned is a division concerning the attribute of the ruling of the command, and the attribute of the commanded act itself. As for that which is an attribute subsisting in other than it, i.e., time, it must be arranged on the first level. ***** And this is the chapter on the division of the commanded act concerning the ruling of time.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh discussion on the conditions for the continuation (baqa') of obligations. The author, al-Bazdawi, establishes a key distinction: some obligations require only the condition of 'qudra' (ability) to continue, while others require 'yusr' (ease) as well. He begins with kaffara (expiation). He argues that kaffara is not legislated for enriching the poor; it is for concealment or deterrence. Therefore, it does not require the attribute of wealth (ghina) in the obligated person; only ability and ease are needed. Since enrichment is not the purpose, the obligation continues even if the person becomes unable to enrich, as long as ability and ease exist in a minimal sense. This principle is then applied analogically to 'ushr' (tithe) and 'kharaj' (land tax). The tithe on crops falls if the crop is destroyed because it was obligated with the condition of ability accompanied by ease (yusr). The land tax similarly falls if the crop is destroyed by pestilence. The author then contrasts this with Hajj: once it becomes obligatory through ownership of provisions and mount, it does not fall if those are later lost, because Hajj requires only ability (qudra), not ease (yusr). Ease (servants, mounts) is not a condition by consensus. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr does not fall with loss of wealth or the person, because it was obligated with the condition of ability and eligibility (through wealth), not ease. The passage also distinguishes the effect of debt on different obligations. For sadaqat al-fitr, debt at the time of obligation prevents obligation because it negates the wealth condition. For trade zakat (zakat al-tijara), a slave's debt that is for trade causes the obligation to fall because trade zakat requires complete wealth in the very nisab. The author concludes by noting this is a division concerning the attribute of the command and the commanded act, and then transitions to a new section on the attribute of time.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra): The ability to perform an obligation, a condition for obligation and continuation in all duties.
يسر (yusr): Ease or facility in fulfilling an obligation, an additional condition for continuation of certain obligations beyond mere ability.
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for certain offenses, such as breaking an oath or intentional fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the obligation of Hajj not fall if a person loses the mount and provisions after the obligation becomes due?
A) Because Hajj is once in a lifetime.
B) Because Hajj requires only ability (qudra), not ease (yusr).
C) Because the mount and provisions are not necessary.
D) Because Hajj is not analogous to kaffara.

Key Takeaway
The condition of ease (yusr) determines whether an obligation continues after its original subject matter is lost; kaffara and ushr require yusr, while hajj and sadaqat al-fitr do not.

The Persistence of Obligations Based on Capability
Explaining that Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr do not drop when their conditions are lost.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shart al-qudra and shart al-yusr in Hanafi usul, and apply the rule that obligations triggered by capability do not lapse upon the loss of that condition.

Core Idea
Obligations based on qudra persist; ease is never a condition for their continuance.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul tackles a key Hanafi principle: an obligation that was validly triggered by a condition of capability (qudra) remains binding even after that capability is lost. The author contrasts this with a supposed condition of ease (yusr) and illustrates it through Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr. Understanding this rule prevents the error of assuming that later inability cancels a duty that was already due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The author states a general rule: obligations based on capability (qudra) do not fall away when that capability is lost, as opposed to obligations based on ease (yusr). Locate this claim.
The rule is introduced by contrasting with the previous topic.
2
Examine the Hajj example
The author argues that Hajj becomes obligatory upon possessing provisions and mount (capability), but losing them does not cancel the obligation. Note the reasoning: because the condition was qudra, not yusr.
Ease would require servants, mounts, assistants – not required by consensus.
3
Apply the rule to Sadaqat al-Fitr
Similarly, Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligated by the condition of wealth (ghina) which is a type of capability. Losing wealth afterward does not cancel it; the obligation was not based on ease.
Wealth here means ordinary and work clothes, not luxurious ease.
4
Analyse the debt exceptions
The author distinguishes between debt that negates the condition of obligation at the time of obligation (personal debt prevents wealth) and debt on a slave (does not prevent the owner's wealth from other property). Also, zakat on trade goods lapses if the slave's debt affects the specific nisab.
Focus on the condition of obligation at the moment it becomes due, not later.
5
Summarise the usul principle
Conclude that the attribute of the command (hukm) is based on qudra, not yusr. The condition for obligation need not persist after obligation is established.
This is a core Hanafi usul rule affecting many obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا مخالف للحج، فإنه إذا وجب بملك الزاد والراحلة: لم يسقط بفَوْتهما؛ لأنه وجب بشرط القدرة، دون اليُسر، ألا يُرى أن الزاد والراحلة أدنى ما يُقطع به السفر، ولا يقع اليسر إلا بخدم ومراكب وأعوان، وليس بشرط بالإجماع، فلذلك لم يكن شرطاً لدوام الواجب. وكذلك لا تسقط صدقة الفطر بهلاك الرأس، وذهاب الغنى؛ لأنها لم تجب بصفة اليسر، بل بشرط القدرة، وقيام صفة الأهلية بالغنى، ألا يُرى أنها وجبت بسبب رأس الحر، ولا يقع به الغنى، ووجبت بالغنى بثياب البذلة والمهنة، ولا يقع بها اليسر؛ لأنها ليست بنامية، فلم يكن البقاء مفتقراً إلى دوام شرط الوجوب. ولا يلزم أنها لا تجب عند قيام الدين وقت الوجوب؛ لأن الدين يُعدِم الغنى الذي هو شرط الوجوب، وبه تقع أهلية الإغناء. بخلاف الدين على العبد، فإنه لا يمنع؛ لأنه لا يمنع قيام الغنى بمال آخر يفضل عن حاجته بالغاً مائتي درهم. بخلاف زكاة التجارة، فإنها تسقط بدين العبد الذي هو للتجارة؛ لأن الزكاة تقتضي صفة الغنى الكامل بعين النصاب، لا بغيره، والله أعلم. هذا الذي ذكرنا هو تقسيم في صفة حكم الأمر، وصفة المأمور به في نفسه فأما ما يكون صفةً قائمةً بغيره، وهو الوقت: فلا بد من ترتيبه على الدرجة الأولى.
And this is contrary to Hajj, for if it becomes obligatory by possessing provisions and mount, it does not lapse by their loss; because it became obligatory by the condition of capability, not ease; do you not see that provisions and mount are the minimum by which travel is undertaken, and ease only occurs with servants, mounts, and assistants, and that is not a condition by consensus, therefore it was not a condition for the continuance of the obligation. Likewise, Sadaqat al-Fitr does not lapse by the destruction of the head (i.e. the person) and the loss of wealth; because it was not obligated by the attribute of ease, but by the condition of capability and the establishment of the attribute of eligibility by wealth; do you not see that it became obligatory due to the head of a free person, and wealth does not occur by that, and it became obligatory by wealth consisting of ordinary and work clothes, and ease does not occur by that because they are not productive; so continuance did not depend upon the continuance of the condition of obligation. And it does not follow that it is not obligatory when debt exists at the time of obligation; because debt negates wealth which is the condition of obligation, and by it eligibility for enrichment occurs. Contrary to debt upon the slave, for it does not prevent; because it does not prevent the existence of wealth with another property that exceeds his need, amounting to two hundred dirhams. Contrary to zakat of trade, for it lapses by the debt of the slave that is for trade; because zakat requires the attribute of complete wealth in the very nisab, not other than it. And Allah knows best. This that we have mentioned is a division concerning the attribute of the command's ruling and the attribute of the commanded act in itself. As for what is an attribute subsisting in something else, and that is time: it must be arranged upon the first level.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is from Imam al-Bazdawi's usul al-fiqh. It discusses a rule: obligations that are based on the condition of capability (shart al-qudra) do not become void upon the loss of that condition once the obligation is established. The author contrasts this with obligations based on 'yusr' (ease). For Hajj, the obligation arises upon possessing provisions and a mount, but if one loses them after the obligation is due, the obligation remains; it does not fall away. This is because the condition for obligation was capability (qudra), not ease (yusr). Ease requires servants, mounts, and assistants, which are not conditions for Hajj by consensus. Similarly, Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory upon the head of a free person with the condition of wealth (ghina), but if one becomes poor after the obligation, it does not lapse. This is because the obligation was based on the condition of capability (qudra) and the attribute of eligibility (ahliyya) by wealth at the time of obligation, not on ease. The passage then distinguishes between debt that prevents obligation (debt on oneself nullifies the wealth condition) and debt on a slave (does not prevent because the slave's debt does not negate the owner's wealth from other property). Also, zakat on trade goods lapses by the debt of the slave who is engaged in trade, because trade zakat requires complete wealth in the specific nisab. The author concludes by stating that this discussion was about the attribute of the command itself, and now they will move to time as an attribute of the commanded act.

Key Terms
شَرْط القُدرة (shart al-qudra): A condition that establishes capability, not ease; once the obligation is triggered by this condition, the obligation persists even if the condition is later lost.
اليُسر (al-yusr): Ease or affluence, which is not a condition for obligations like Hajj or Sadaqat al-Fitr; it requires a higher level of comfort.
الغنى (al-ghina): Wealth or sufficiency; a condition for obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr, but once obligation occurs, loss of wealth does not cancel it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Sadaqat al-Fitr not lapse by the destruction of the head (person) and the loss of wealth after obligation?
A) Because it was based on ease (yusr), which is a lasting condition.
B) Because it was based on the condition of capability (qudra) and eligibility through wealth, not ease.
C) Because the head of a free person is always valuable.
D) Because wealth only needs to be present at the time of performance.

Key Takeaway
Obligations in Hanafi usul that are triggered by a condition of capability remain binding even after the condition is lost, as long as the obligation was validly established at its time.

The First Part of Time as Cause for Obligation
Explaining that the initial part of time is the cause for obligation in time-bound acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why, in Hanafi usul, only a part of time is designated as the cause (sabab) for obligation in time-bound acts, and distinguish between the occurrence of obligation (wujub) and the address for performance (khitab).

Core Idea
Obligation begins with the first part of time, but performance is deferred until demand.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses a foundational Hanafi rule: in time-bound acts like daily prayers, the entire time cannot be the cause for obligation. Instead, a part of time – specifically the earliest part – serves as the cause. The author establishes this with evidence from the rulings on disbelievers and menstruating women, and then clarifies a crucial distinction between the obligation itself (wujub) and the command to perform (khitab), which is delayed until near the end of the time. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the logical problem
If the whole time were the cause, performance would either precede the cause or be delayed after it, which is irrational. Therefore, only a part can be the cause.
This is the core argument.
2
Identify which part is designated
The part immediately preceding performance is made the cause, and since there is no specific part after the whole, the least (i.e., the beginning) is chosen.
The author argues for the initial part as most deserving.
3
Analyze the textual evidence
Imam Muhammad's report about a menstruating woman: if she catches any part of the time, prayer becomes obligatory. This shows that a part, not the whole, triggers obligation.
The disbeliever case similarly shows obligation by catching the last part.
4
Distinguish wujub from khitab
Obligation (wujub) arises immediately from the first part, but the address (khitab) commanding performance is deferred. This is analogous to a sale price – obligation at contract, but performance only upon demand.
This resolves the apparent tension.
5
Contrast with alternative positions
Some Hanafis denied obligation at the first part; al-Shafi'i held khitab is immediate. The author rebuts with the absence of demand from the Lawgiver.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوجوبه، وذلك مثل شهر رمضان. والقسم الثالث: ما جعل الوقت معياراً له، ولم يُجعل سبباً له، مثل أوقات صيام القضاء، والكفارات، والنذور. والأصل في أنواع القسم الأول من المؤقتة: أن الوقت لما جعل سبباً لوجوبها، وظرفاً لأدائها: لم يستقم أن يكون كل الوقت سبباً؛ لأن ذلك يوجب تأخير الأداء عن وقته، أو تقديمه على سببه، فوجب أن يُجعل بعضه سبباً، وهو ما يسبق الأداء، حتى يقع الأداء بعد سببه، وليس بعد الكل جزء مقدر، فوجب الاقتصار على الأدنى. ولهذا قالوا في الكافر: إذا أدرك الجزء الأخير بعد ما أسلم: لزمه فرض الوقت. وقد قال محمد رحمه الله في نوادر الصلاة في مسألة الحائض إذا طهرت وأيامها عشرة: إن الصلاة تلزمها إذا أدركت شيئاً من الوقت، قليلاً كان ذلك أو كثيراً. وإذا ثبت هذا كان الجزء السابق أولى أن يُجعل سبباً؛ لعدم ما يزاحمه، وبدليل أن الأداء بعد الجزء الأول: صحيح، ولولا أنه سببٌ: لَمَا صح. ولما صار الجزء الأول سبباً أفاد الوجوب بنفسه، وأفاد صحة الأداء للحال؛ لأن الوجوب جبر من الله تعالى بلا اختيار من العبد. ثم إنه ليس من ضرورة الوجوب تعجيل الأداء، بل الأداء متراخ إلى الطلب كثمن المبيع ومهر النكاح يجبان بالعقد، ووجوب الأداء يتأخر إلى المطالبة، وهو الخطاب، وأما الوجوب فبالإيجاب؛ لصحة سببه، لا بالخطاب. ولهذا كانت الاستطاعة مقارنةً للفعل، وهو: كثوب هبَّت به الريح فألقته في دار إنسان لا يجب عليه تسليمه إلا بالطلب. وفي مسألتنا لم توجد المطالبة بدلالة أن الشرع خيره في وقت الأداء، فلا يلزمه الأداء إلا أن يسقط خياره بضيق الوقت. ولهذا قلنا: إذا مات قبل آخر الوقت لا شيء عليه، وهو كالنائم، والمغمى عليه إذا مرَّ عليهما جميعُ وقت الصلاة وجب الأصل، وتراخى وجوب الأداء، والخطاب، فكذلك عن الجزء الأول. وتبيّن أن الوجوب يحصلُ بأول الجزء، خلافاً لبعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله، وأن الخطاب بالأداء لا يتعجل، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله. ثم إذا انقضى الجزء الأول، فلم يؤد: انتقلت السببية إلى الجزء الثاني، كذلك تنتقل؛ لما قلنا؛ لِمَا قلنا من ضرورة تقدُّم السبب على وقت الأداء، وكان ما يلي الأداء به أولى؛ لأنه لما وجب نقل السببية عن الجملة إلى الأقل: لم يجز تقريره على جميع ما سَبَقَ قبيل الأداء؛ لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى التخطي عن القليل بلا دليل. وإذا انتهى إلى آخر الوقت حتى تعيَّن الأداء لازماً: استقرت السببية لما يلي الشروع في الأداء، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً، كما في الفجر وجب كاملاً، فإذا اعترض الفساد بطلوع الشمس: بطل الفرض.
And for its obligation, such as the month of Ramadan. The third type: that which makes time a standard for it, and does not make it a cause for it, like the times of fasting for make-up, expiations, and vows. The principle concerning the types of the first type of time-bound acts: that when time is made a cause for their obligation and a vessel for their performance, it is not correct that the entire time be a cause, because that would necessitate delaying performance from its time or advancing it before its cause. So it is necessary that some part of it be made a cause, namely the part that precedes performance, so that performance occurs after its cause. And since there is no specific part after the whole, it is necessary to limit to the least. For this reason they said concerning the disbeliever: if he catches the last part after he becomes Muslim, the obligatory prayer of that time becomes incumbent upon him. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in Nawadir al-Salat concerning the issue of a menstruating woman if she becomes pure and her days are ten: that prayer becomes obligatory upon her if she catches any part of the time, little or much. And if this is established, then the preceding part is more deserving to be made a cause, due to the absence of any impediment, and by evidence that performance after the first part is valid, and if it were not a cause, it would not be valid. And when the first part becomes a cause, it necessitates obligation by itself and necessitates the validity of performance immediately, because obligation is a compulsion from Allah Almighty without choice of the servant. Then, it is not necessary from obligation to hasten performance, rather performance is deferred until demand, like the price of a sold item and the dowry of marriage, which become obligatory by the contract, and the obligation of performance is delayed until demand, which is the address. As for obligation, it is by legislation due to the validity of its cause, not by address. For this reason, capacity (istita'ah) is concurrent with the act, such as a garment blown by the wind that lands in a person's house, he is not obligated to return it except by demand. In our case, there is no demand, indicated by the fact that the Law gives him choice in the time of performance, so he is not obligated to perform unless his choice falls away due to the time becoming narrow. For this reason we said: if he dies before the end of the time, nothing is due upon him. It is like the sleeping person and the unconscious person: if the entire time of prayer passes over them, the origin (asl) becomes obligatory, and the obligation of performance and the address are deferred, so likewise concerning the first part. And it becomes clear that obligation occurs at the beginning of the part, contrary to some of our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them), and that the address concerning performance is not hastened, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). Then, when the first part passes and he did not perform, causality transfers to the second part, and so on, for what we said, due to the necessity of the cause preceding the time of performance, and what is adjacent to performance is more deserving; because when it was necessary to transfer causality from the whole to the least, it is not permissible to settle it on all of what preceded just before performance, because that leads to bypassing the least without evidence. And when it reaches the end of the time such that performance becomes determined and necessary, causality settles on what is adjacent to the commencement of performance. If that part is sound, as in Fajr, it becomes obligatory in full, and if corruption intervenes by sunrise, the obligation becomes void.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of an usul rule regarding how time becomes a cause (sabab) for obligatory acts in the Hanafi school. The author discusses the first of three types of time-bound acts (muwaqqat): where time is both the cause for obligation and the vessel for performance, as in the month of Ramadan. He argues that the entire time cannot be the cause because that would lead to absurdity (delay or advancement of performance). Instead, only a part of the time must be designated as the cause, specifically the part immediately preceding performance. This is proven by the ruling that a disbeliever who embraces Islam during the last part of the time is obligated to pray, and by Imam Muhammad's statement in Nawadir al-Salat that a menstruating woman upon purification is obligated for the prayer if she catches any part of the time. Once the first part becomes the cause, it brings about the obligation (wujub) immediately, but the performance (ada') is deferred until the demand (talab) or address (khitab) is present. This is analogous to a sale price or dowry: their obligation occurs at the contract, but the duty to pay is deferred until demand. Hence, one does not sin by delaying performance until the end of the time, and if one dies before the end, no penalty applies. The author then contrasts his view with some of his teachers who held differently on the timing of obligation, and with al-Shafi'i who apparently held that the address for performance is immediate. Finally, the passage explains how causality transfers through the parts of time until performance is executed or the time expires, using Fajr prayer as a case where sunrise invalidates the prayer if not performed before.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): That which necessitates the ruling (hukm) in the sense of making it obligatory, but does not directly cause performance.
الوجوب (al-wujub): The legal obligation (fardiyyah) that attaches to the act once the cause is present, regardless of the ability to perform immediately.
الخطاب (al-khitab): The explicit address from the Lawgiver commanding performance, which is delayed until the time for performance becomes specific.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the obligation (wujub) of a time-bound act such as Fajr prayer occur?
A) At the very beginning of the entire time slot.
B) At the last part of the time slot.
C) Only when performance is actually begun.
D) After the address (khitab) is issued by the Lawgiver.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, for time-bound obligations, the cause (sabab) is the first part of time, not the whole, and the obligation to perform (khitab) is deferred until the end of the time.

The Nature of Obligation and Transfer of Causality Across Time
Analyzing how obligation relates to cause and address, and how causality transfers across parts of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between obligation (wujub) arising from a cause (sabab) and the address (khitab) to perform, and explain how causality transfers across parts of time in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Obligation is fixed by the cause, not the address; the demand to perform is deferred and transfers across time.

In Hanafi usul, a key distinction is made between the obligation itself (wujub) and the command to perform (khitab). The obligation arises from a sound cause (sabab), while the performance demand may be deferred. This passage applies this distinction to the prayer times, explaining how causality transfers across parts of time until performance is mandatory. Understanding this transfer is crucial for correctly judging the validity of prayers that extend into prohibited times.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between wujub and khitab
Identify from the text that obligation (wujub) is established by a sound cause (e.g., contract for sale, entrance of prayer time), not by the address (khitab). The address is the demand to perform, which may be deferred. Note the example of price/dower and the wind-blown garment.
2
Apply the distinction to prayer time
The entire prayer time is a cause (sabab) for obligation, but the command to perform is not immediate. The worshipper has choice within the time; if the time passes without performance, the obligation remains but performance is deferred. Use the examples of the sleeper, unconscious person, and one who dies before the end.
3
Trace the transfer of causality (sababiyyah)
As each part of the time passes without performance, the causality transfers to the next part, eventually concentrating on the part adjacent to actual performance. When performance begins, the cause settles on that part. If that part is valid (e.g., dawn prayer before sunrise), obligation is complete; if invalid (e.g., Asr at sunset), the obligation is diminished but performance is still valid due to excusable invalidity (afw).
The transfer necessity is to ensure the cause precedes the act.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf and thamarah
Some Hanafi mashā'ikh held that obligation occurs at the first part; al-Shāfi'ī held that the address is immediate. The author argues against both: the Lawgiver's granting of choice shows deferral. The practical difference: If one begins Asr at the beginning and finishes after sunset, Hanafi maintains validity (afw) while Shāfi'ī would rule invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطلب كثمن المبيع ومهر النكاح يجبان بالعقد، ووجوب الأداء يتأخر إلى المطالبة، وهو الخطاب، وأما الوجوب فبالإيجاب؛ لصحة سببه، لا بالخطاب. ولهذا كانت الاستطاعة مقارنةً للفعل، وهو: كثوب هبَّت به الريح فألقته في دار إنسان لا يجب عليه تسليمه إلا بالطلب. وفي مسألتنا لم توجد المطالبة بدلالة أن الشرع خيره في وقت الأداء، فلا يلزمه الأداء إلا أن يسقط خياره بضيق الوقت. ولهذا قلنا : إذا مات قبل آخر الوقت لا شيء عليه، وهو كالنائم، والمغمى عليه إذا مرَّ عليهما جميعُ وقت الصلاة وجب الأصل، وتراخى وجوب الأداء، والخطاب، فكذلك عن الجزء الأول. وتبيّن أن الوجوب يحصلُ بأول الجزء، خلافاً لبعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله، وأن الخطاب بالأداء لا يتعجل، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله. ثم إذا انقضى الجزء الأول، فلم يؤد : انتقلت السببية إلى الجزء الثاني، كذلك تنتقل ؛ لما قلنا ؛ لِمَا قلنا من ضرورة تقدُّم السبب على وقت الأداء، وكان ما يلي الأداء به أولى؛ لأنه لما وجب نقل السببية عن الجملة إلى الأقل : لم يجز تقريره على جميع ما سَبَقَ قبيل الأداء ؛ لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى التخطي عن القليل بلا دليل. وإذا انتهى إلى آخر الوقت حتى تعيَّن الأداء لازماً: استقرت السببية لما يلي الشروع في الأداء، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً، كما في الفجر وجب كاملاً، فإذا اعترض الفساد بطلوع الشمس : بطل الفرض. وإذا كان ذلك الجزء فاسداً : انتقص الواجب، كالعصر تُستأنف في وقت الاحمرار، فإذا غربت الشمس وهو فيها : لم يتغير، ولم تفسد. ولا يلزم إذا ابتدأ العصر في أول الوقت، ثم مده إلى أن غربت الشمس قبل فراغه منها فإنه نص محمد أنه لا تفسد، وقد كان الوجوب مضافاً إلى سبب صحيح. ووجهه أن الشرع جعل الوقت متّسعاً، ولكن جعل له حق شغل كل الوقت بالأداء، فإذا شغله بالأداء : جاز وإن اتصل به الفساد ؛ لأن ما يتصل به من الفساد بالبناء: جعل عفواً ؛ لأن الاحتراز عنه مع الإقبال على الصلاة متعذر. وقد روى هشام عن محمد رحمهما الله فيمن قام إلى الخامسة في العصر : أنه يستحب له الإتمام؛ لأنه من غير قصده ثبت، فإذا اتصل به الفساد : صار في الحكم عفواً، فصار بمنزلة المؤدى في وقت الصحة. بخلاف حالة الابتداء ؛ لأنه بقصده ثبت الفساد، إذ الاحتراز عنه ممكن، بأن يختار وقتاً لا فساد فيه. وأما إذا خلا الوقت عن الأداء أصلاً : فقد ذهبت الضرورة الداعية إلى نقل السببية عن الكل إلى الجزء، وهو ما ذكرنا من شغل الأداء، فانتقل الحكم إلى ما هو الأصل، وهو أن يُجعل كل الوقت سبباً، فإذا فاتت العصر أصلاً أضيف وجوبها إلى جملة الوقت، دون الجزء الفاسد، فوجبت بصفة الكمال، فلم يجز أداؤها بصفة النقصان. ولا يلزم إذا أسلم الكافرُ في آخر وقت العصر، ثم لم يُؤدِّ حتى احمرَّت الشمس في اليوم الثاني، وقد نسي، ثم تذكرها، فأراد أن يؤديها
The demand like the price of a sale and the dower of marriage are obligatory by the contract, and the obligation of performance is deferred to the demand, which is the address. As for the obligation, it is by the cause due to the soundness of its cause, not by the address. For this reason, ability is concomitant with the act, like a garment blown by the wind into a person's house, which he is not obligated to return except upon demand. In our issue, the demand does not exist, indicated by the fact that the Law gave him a choice in the time of performance, so performance is not incumbent upon him unless his choice is nullified by the time becoming too short. For this we said: If he dies before the end of the time, nothing is upon him, and it is like the sleeper and the unconscious one if the entire time of prayer passes over them—the original obligation is established, but the obligation of performance and the address are deferred. Similarly for the first part. And it is clear that the obligation occurs at the beginning of the part, contrary to some of our mashā'ikh, may Allah have mercy on them, and that the address for performance is not hastened, contrary to al-Shāfi'ī, may Allah have mercy on him. Then if the first part passes and he has not performed, the causality transfers to the second part, and so on, because of what we said about the necessity of the cause preceding the time of performance, and what is adjacent to performance is more deserving; for when it became necessary to transfer causality from the whole to the lesser, it is not permissible to retain it for all that preceded performance, because that would lead to skipping the lesser without evidence. And when it reaches the end of the time so that performance becomes determined as obligatory, the causality is established for what is adjacent to the beginning of performance. If that part is valid, as in the dawn prayer, it becomes obligatory completely, and if invalidity intervenes by sunrise, the obligation is voided. If that part is invalid, the obligation is diminished, like the afternoon prayer which is recommenced at the time of redness; if the sun sets while he is in it, it does not change and does not become invalid. And it is not necessary that if one begins the afternoon prayer at the beginning of its time and then extends it until the sun sets before he finishes it, for Muhammad explicitly stated that it does not become invalid, and the obligation was attached to a sound cause. Its explanation: The Law made the time expansive, but gave it the right to occupy all the time with performance; if he occupies it with performance, it is permissible even if invalidity is connected to it, because what is connected of invalidity by building upon is made excusable, because avoiding it while focusing on prayer is difficult. Hishām related from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, about one who stands for a fifth [rak'ah] in the afternoon prayer: that it is recommended for him to complete it, because it occurred without his intention, so if invalidity is connected, it becomes in effect excusable, and it becomes like that performed in a valid time. Unlike the state of beginning, because invalidity is established by his intention, since avoidance is possible by choosing a time without invalidity. As for when the time is completely empty of performance, then the necessity that required transferring causality from the whole to the part has disappeared—that is, the occupation of performance—so the ruling reverts to the original, which is that the entire time is made the cause. So if the afternoon prayer is missed entirely, its obligation is attached to the entire time, not to the invalid part, so it becomes obligatory in its complete form, and it is not permissible to perform it in a diminished form. And it is not necessary that if a disbeliever embraces Islam at the end of the afternoon prayer's time and then does not perform until the sun reddens on the second day, having forgotten, then remembers and wishes to perform it...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a discourse on the nature of obligation (wujub) and the distinction between obligation arising from the cause (sabab) and the address (khitab) commanding performance. The author begins by establishing a general principle: obligations such as the price in a sale or the dower in marriage become binding by the contract (the cause), but the duty to actually pay is deferred until demand (the address). Similarly, ability (istita'ah) is concomitant with the act, not prior. The example of a garment blown by wind into a house illustrates that the owner is not obliged to return it without a demand. This is then applied to the prayer: the entire time of a prayer is the cause of obligation, but the command to perform is not immediate; the worshipper has a choice within the time. If he dies before the end, nothing is owed, just as a sleeper or unconscious person is not liable if the whole time passes. The author disagrees with some Hanafi scholars who disagree about the precise moment of obligation, and with al-Shafi'i who holds that the address for performance is immediate. The causal connection (sababiyya) is then described as transferring from the whole time to the part adjacent to actual performance. As the time passes without performance, the cause shifts to the next part, and so on, until the last part where performance becomes mandatory. If performance is begun in a valid part and completed in an invalid one (e.g., Asr prayer at sunset), the prayer is valid and not invalid, based on a report from Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is because the invalidity that attaches to the end is excusable (afw) due to the difficulty of avoiding it once engaged. Conversely, if no performance occurs at all, the cause reverts to the entire time, and the prayer must be made up in its complete form. The passage ends with a beginning of a case about a convert who misses the prayer, leaving the ruling implied.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): The legal obligation that arises from a sound cause, distinct from the command to perform (khitab).
السببية (al-sababiyyah): The causal relationship between the time of prayer and the obligation; it can transfer from the whole time to parts of it.
الخطاب (al-khitab): The address or command to perform the obligated act; it is distinct from the obligation itself and may be deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone begins the Asr prayer at the beginning of its time and continues until sunset before finishing, based on the text from Muhammad?
A) The prayer becomes invalid because it extends into the prohibited time.
B) The prayer remains valid because the invalidity that attaches is excused.
C) The prayer is void and must be repeated as qada.
D) The prayer is valid only if the person intended to finish before sunset.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to perform is not immediate; it transfers across time parts, and invalidity at the end is excused if performance began in a sound cause.

Rules of Time and Obligation in Hanafi Usul
Lists general rulings derived from principles of time and obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the six derived rules about time, intention, and obligation from the principle that the time of performance is not legally specified.

Core Idea
The servant cannot specify time by intention alone; specification happens through performance.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul lists several important legal consequences (ahkam) that follow from the key principle that the time for performing obligations is not fixed by the servant. These rules cover how obligations become specified, the role of intention, the effect of delay, and the relationship between time and multiple obligations. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying Hanafi usul to issues of prayer times and expiations.

Guided Path
1
Rule on ta'yin (specification) by performance
The passage states that specification of which prayer (e.g., Zuhr vs. Asr) is not achieved by mere intention or verbal declaration; rather, it is determined by the actual performance itself. This is analogous to expiation for oaths where one must actually perform one of the options for it to count.
Analogy with kaffarah: intention alone does not specify which option; action does.
2
Rule on fawat (loss) due to delay
Delaying the prayer beyond its time causes fawat—the condition of performance (time) is lost, so the obligation becomes qada.
Fawat means the act becomes due as qada.
3
Rule on non-negation of other prayers
Time as a container (zarf) for an obligation does not negate other obligations; each prayer has its own time and right. The time remains 'empty' for other prayers.
Applies to multiple prayers within the same time frame (e.g., making up missed prayers).
4
Rule on intention (niyyah) as condition
Intention is required to direct the physical act (what is his) to the obligation upon him (what is upon him). Without niyyah, the act does not fulfill the obligation.
Niyyah distinguishes worship from habit.
5
Rule on specification of intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) and its persistence
When multiple obligations exist, one must specify which one is being performed (e.g., 'I intend to pray Zuhr'). This ta'yin is not dropped even if the time is narrow; the expansiveness of time actually adds this condition.
Common mistake: thinking narrow time allows omitting ta'yin. The text says the opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن حُكْم هذا القسم: أن وقت الأداء لما لم يكن متعيناً شرعاً، والاختيار فيه للعبد : لم يُقبل التعين بتعيينه قصداً ونصاً، وإنما يتعين ضرورة تعيّن الأداء، وهذا لأن تعين الشرط أو السبب ضرب تصرُّف فيه، وليس إلى العبد ولاية وضع الأسباب والشروط ، فصار إثبات ولاية التعيين ينزع إلى الشركة في وضع المشروعات وإنما إلى العبد أن يرتفق قصداً بما هو حقه، ثم يتعين به المشروع حكماً. ونظير هذا الكفارة الواجبة فى الأيمان، أن الحانث فيها بالخيار: إن شاء أطعم عشرة مساكين، وإن شاء كساهم وإن شاء حرَّر رقبةً، ولو عيَّن ذلك قصداً : لم يصح ، وإنما يصح ضرورة فعله؛ لما قلنا. ومن حكمه أن التأخير عن الوقت: يوجب الفوات؛ لذهاب شرط الأداء. ومن حكم كونه ظرفاً للواجب : أنه لا ينفي غيره ؛ لأنه مشروع أفعالاً معلومةً في ذمة مَن عليه فبقي الوقت خالياً، وبقيت منافعه على حقه، فلم ينتف غيرها من الصلوات. ومن حكمه : أن النية شرط ليصير ما له مصروفاً إلى ما عليه. ومن حكمه : أن تعيين النية شرط؛ لأن المشروع لما تعدد : لم يصر مذكوراً بالاسم المطلق إلا عند تعيين الوصف. ومن حكمه أنه لما لزمه التعيين لما قلنا : لم يسقط بضيق وقت الأداء؛ لأن التوسعة أفادت شرطاً زائداً وهو التعيين، فلا يسقط هذا.
And from the rulings of this section: that since the time of performance is not legally specified [in detail], and the choice is for the servant, specification by his intention and explicit statement is not accepted; rather it is specified by the necessity of the performance itself. Because specification of the condition or cause is a type of disposition in it, and the servant has no authority to place causes and conditions, so establishing the authority of specification would imply sharing in the legislation of enactments. Rather, the servant has only the right to benefit intentionally from what is his right; then the legislated act becomes specified in effect. Analogous to this is the expiation obligatory for oaths: the one who breaks an oath has a choice: if he wishes, he may feed ten poor people, or clothe them, or free a slave. If he specifies one of these by intention, it is not valid; only by the actual act does it become valid—for the reason we mentioned. And from its rulings: that delay beyond the time necessitates loss (fawat) because the condition of performance is gone. And from the ruling that time is a container for the obligatory: it does not negate other [prayers]; because it is legislated for known actions upon the liability of the person, so the time remains empty, and its benefits remain his right, so other prayers are not negated. And from its rulings: that intention is a condition so that what is his (i.e., the act) is directed to what is upon him (i.e., the obligation). And from its rulings: that specification of intention is a condition; because when the legislated act is multiple, it is not known by the absolute name except when the description is specified. And from its rulings: that since specification became necessary for the reason we mentioned, it does not fall due to narrowness of the time of performance; because the expansiveness added an extra condition—specification—so this does not fall away.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage enumerates several derived rules (ahkam) from the earlier discussion. First, the time for performance is not legally fixed in detail by the servant; the specification of which prayer (e.g., Asr) is determined by the actual performance, not by intention alone. The analogy to expiation (kaffarah) for oaths clarifies: one must actually perform one of the options (feed, clothe, free slave) for it to count; specifying by mere intention without action is insufficient. Second, delaying the prayer beyond its time causes fawat (loss), meaning the obligation becomes qada. Third, time as a container for worship does not negate other prayers; each prayer has its own time slot and rights. Fourth, intention (niyyah) is a condition to distinguish obligatory from voluntary. Fifth, specification of intention (ta'yin) is a condition because multiple obligations exist; one must specify which prayer. Sixth, this specification is not dropped even if the time is narrow; the expansiveness of time adds the requirement of specification. These are foundational usul principles regarding the role of time in obligations.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the particular obligatory act (e.g., which prayer) in intention.
نية (niyyah): Intention to distinguish the act from others and to dedicate it to Allah.
فوات (fawat): Loss of the opportunity to perform in time, leading to qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if a person delays a prayer beyond its time?
A) The obligation becomes void.
B) The condition of performance is lost, necessitating qada.
C) The prayer can still be performed in the same time.
D) The person must perform extra nafl prayers.

Key Takeaway
The six derived rules show that time's legal status (unspecified) governs how obligations are specified, performed, and made up, with the servant's role limited to actual performance.

Time as a Container: Why Intention Cannot Fix the Time
Defines rulings for time as a container in muwaqqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in the first type of time-bound obligations, specification of time by intention is invalid, and explain the qiyas with expiation for oaths.

Core Idea
In time-bound worship where time is a container, only actual performance fixes the time, not intention.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul clarifies a key principle: when the law gives the servant choice over the time of performance, the servant cannot fix that time by mere intention or explicit statement. Instead, the time is determined only by the actual act of worship. This ruling has significant implications for intention (niyyah) and the validity of acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that this passage concerns the first type of muwaqqat (time-bound obligations) where time is a mere container (zarf), not a cause.
The author distinguishes this from the second type where time is a measure and cause.
2
State the central ruling
Since the time is not legally fixed and choice is with the servant, the servant's intention or explicit specification does not fix the time; only actual performance determines it.
The phrase 'تعين ضرورة تعين الأداء' encapsulates this.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The author compares this to expiation for broken oaths, where the servant has a choice among alternatives, and intention alone does not specify which action fulfills the obligation; only the actual action does.
The asl is kaffarah al-yamin; the far is muwaqqat of the first type.
4
List additional rulings
Note that delay causes loss of the act; the time being a container does not exclude other prayers; intention and specifying intention are conditions; specification does not fall away due to time constraints.
These stem from the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند احمرار الشمس؛ لأن هذا لا يُروى.
ومن حُكْم هذا القسم: أن وقت الأداء لما لم يكن متعيناً شرعاً، والاختيار فيه للعبد : لم يُقبل التعين بتعيينه قصداً ونصاً، وإنما يتعين ضرورة تعيّن الأداء، وهذا لأن تعين الشرط أو السبب ضرب تصرُّف فيه، وليس إلى العبد ولاية وضع الأسباب والشروط ، فصار إثبات ولاية التعيين ينزع إلى الشركة في وضع المشروعات وإنما إلى العبد أن يرتفق قصداً بما هو حقه، ثم يتعين به المشروع حكماً.
ونظير هذا الكفارة الواجبة فى الأيمان، أن الحانث فيها بالخيار: إن شاء أطعم عشرة مساكين، وإن شاء كساهم وإن شاء حرَّر رقبةً، ولو عيَّن ذلك قصداً : لم يصح ، وإنما يصح ضرورة فعله؛ لما قلنا.
ومن حكمه أن التأخير عن الوقت: يوجب الفوات؛ لذهاب شرط الأداء.
ومن حكم كونه ظرفاً للواجب : أنه لا ينفي غيره ؛ لأنه مشروع أفعالاً معلومةً في ذمة مَن عليه فبقي الوقت خالياً، وبقيت منافعه على حقه، فلم ينتف غيرها من الصلوات.
*
ومن حكمه : أن النية شرط ليصير ما له مصروفاً إلى ما عليه.
ومن حكمه : أن تعيين النية شرط؛ لأن المشروع لما تعدد : لم يصر مذكوراً بالاسم المطلق إلا عند تعيين الوصف.
ومن حكمه أنه لما لزمه التعيين لما قلنا : لم يسقط بضيق وقت الأداء؛ لأن التوسعة أفادت شرطاً زائداً وهو التعيين، فلا يسقط هذا الشرط بالعوارض، ولا بتقصير العباد.
At the reddening of the sun, because this is not narrated.
And from the ruling of this category: that since the time of performance is not legally determined, and the choice in it belongs to the servant, determination by his intention and explicit expression is not accepted; rather, it is necessarily determined by the necessity of performance. This is because determining a condition or cause is a type of disposal in it, and the servant has no authority to establish causes and conditions. Thus, proving the authority of determination leads to partnership in establishing legislated matters. The servant only has the right to intend to benefit from what is his right, then the legislated act is determined by that as a legal effect.
An analogy for this is the obligatory expiation in oaths: the one who breaks an oath has a choice: if he wishes, he may feed ten poor people; if he wishes, he may clothe them; or if he wishes, he may free a slave. If he specifically intends that (determination), it is not valid; rather, it becomes valid only by necessity of his action, for what we have said.
From its ruling: that delay beyond the time causes loss (of the act), because the condition of performance is gone.
From its ruling: that being a container for the obligation does not negate other acts, because it is legislated for specific actions that are a liability on the one who owes it, so the time remains empty, and its benefits remain his right, so other prayers are not negated.
*
From its ruling: that intention is a condition so that what is his (the performance) is directed towards what he owes.
From its ruling: that specifying the intention is a condition, because when the legislated act is multiple, it is not mentioned by the absolute name except when the attribute is specified.
From its ruling: that since specification became incumbent for what we said, it does not fall away due to the narrowness of the time of performance, because expansion provided an additional condition, namely specification, so this condition is not waived by impediments or by the servant's shortcomings.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings of the first type of time-bound obligations, where time is a pure container (zarf) for the act of worship, not its cause. The author, al-Bazdawi, explains that the time for performance is not fixed by law but left to the servant's choice. Therefore, the servant cannot fix the time by mere intention or explicit statement; it is only fixed by the actual performance. This is because establishing conditions is not within the servant's authority. An analogy is given with the expiation for broken oaths, where the servant has a choice among alternatives but cannot specify the type by intention alone; it is determined by the actual act performed. Other rulings: delay causes the act to be missed because the condition of time is lost; the time being a container does not exclude other prayers, as the servant still has time for other obligations; intention and specification of intention are conditions; and the condition of specification does not fall away even if time is short, because it is a benefit from the expanded time.

Key Terms
الظرف (al-zarf): Time as a mere container for the act of worship, not its cause or condition for validity.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying a particular time or type of act by intention or explicit statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is specification of time by intention alone invalid for the first type of time-bound obligations?
A) Because time is not a condition for the act
B) Because the servant has no authority to establish causes and conditions
C) Because the time is already determined by law
D) Because intention is never required

Key Takeaway
In the first type of muwaqqat, intention cannot fix the time; only actual performance determines the act.
