When Time Is Both Measure and Cause: The Traveler's Fast in Ramadan
Explains the second type where time is both measure and cause, with a dispute on traveler fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a traveler's fasting in Ramadan for a missed fast and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
When time is both measure and cause, it excludes other acts; Sahibayn deny substitution, Abu Hanifa allows it.

In Usul al-Fiqh, obligations can be tied to time in different ways. This lesson examines the second type, where time serves both as a measure (mi'yar) to determine the quantity of the obligation and as a cause (sabab) for its obligation. The prime example is Ramadan fasting. The key question: if a traveler is given a concession to not fast in Ramadan, can he instead fast to make up a missed Ramadan? Abu Hanifa and his two disciples disagree, revealing a deeper usul principle about the exclusivity of the time-based obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time category
Recognize that the text describes time as both mi'yar (measure) and sabab (cause). Ramadan is the measure for fasting (the amount is fixed by it) and the cause (witnessing part of the month triggers obligation).
This is the second type of time-bound obligations (muwaqqatah).
2
Understand the negation rule
The text states that when the law fills the measure with one specific act, other acts are negated. Analogous to measured goods: the measure (e.g., a cup) is filled with one item, excluding others. Thus, during Ramadan, only the Ramadan fast is legislated.
This is a key usul principle: once the measure is occupied, others are excluded.
3
Contrast the two positions
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that since only Ramadan fasting is legislated in this time, a traveler cannot fast for any other purpose (e.g., a missed Ramadan). Abu Hanifa holds that the obligation is binding on the traveler, and the concession allows him to leave the Ramadan fast, but he may choose the resolve (azima) and fast for another obligation.
Focus on the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each view.
4
Analyze the evidence and analogy
The Sahibayn use a qiyas: just as a measure excludes other goods, Ramadan excludes other fasts. Abu Hanifa counters by distinguishing: the concession is for leaving the fast, not for substitution; if the traveler chooses to fast, he can fulfill his religious duty (qada) because that serves his religious interest, just as he may take a bodily concession.
Note the istihsani element in Abu Hanifa's reasoning.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
The disagreement leads to a concrete difference: according to Abu Hanifa, a traveler who fasts in Ramadan intending to make up a missed Ramadan will have that fast valid and count toward his missed obligation. According to the Sahibayn, the fast is invalid because his intention is for a non-legislated act.
This thamarah affects the ruling for the individual's religious duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النوع الثاني من المؤقتة فما جعل الوقت معياراً له، وسبباً لوجوبه، مثل شهر رمضان.
وإنما قلنا إنه معيار له ؛ لأنه قُدَّر وعُرف به ، وسبب له، وذلك شهودُ جزء من الشهر ؛ على ما نذكر في باب السبب إن شاء الله تعالى.
ومن حكمه: أن غيره صار منفياً؛ لأن الشرع لما أوجب شغل المعيار به، وهو واحد، فإذا ثبت له وصف: انتفى غيره، كالمكيل والموزون في معياره، فانتفى غيره ؛ لكونه غير مشروع.
قال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : ولما لم يبقَ غيره مشروعاً : لم يجز أداء الواجب فيه من المسافر ؛ لأن شَرْع الصوم فيه عام.
ألا يُرى أن صوم المسافر عن الفرض يجزئه، فثبت أنه مشروع في حقه، إلا أنه رُخص له أن يدعه بالفطر، وهذا لا يجعل غير الفرض مشروعاً، فانعدم فعله؛ لعدم ما نواه.
وكذلك على قولهما : إذا نوى النفل، أو أطلق النية.
وكذلك المريض في هذا كله.
وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : الوجوب واقع على المسافر، ولهذا صح أداؤه بلا توقف إلا أنه رُخص له الترك ؛ قضاء لحقه، وتخفيفاً عليه، فلما ساغ له الترخص بما يرجع إلى مصالح بدنه : ففيما يرجع إلى مصالح دينه - قضاء ما عليه من الدين - أولى، وصار كونه ناسخاً لغيره متعلقاً بإعراضه عن جهة الرخصة، وتمسكه بالعزيمة وإذا لم يفعل بقي
As for the second type of time-bound obligations, it is that which is made a measure for it and a cause for its obligation, such as the month of Ramadan.
We only said it is a measure for it because it is estimated and known by it, and a cause for it, and that is by witnessing a part of the month, as we will mention in the chapter on cause, God willing.
From its ruling: that other (acts) are negated; because when the law obligated filling the measure with it, and it is one, then when the description is established for it, other (acts) are negated, like the measured and weighed in their measure, so other (acts) are negated because they are not legislated.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may God have mercy on them) said: And when nothing else remains legislated, it is not permissible for the traveler to perform the obligation in it (i.e., fast a different obligation), because the legislation of fasting (Ramadan) is general.
Do you not see that the traveler's fast for the obligation (of Ramadan) suffices him? So it is established that it is legislated for him, except that he is permitted to leave it by not fasting, and this does not make something other than the obligation (i.e., a voluntary fast) legislated, so his action is void due to the absence of what he intended.
And similarly according to their statement: if he intended a voluntary (fast), or made an absolute intention.
And similarly the sick person in all this.
Abu Hanifa (may God have mercy on him) said: The obligation is binding on the traveler, and therefore his performance (of the Ramadan fast) is valid without pause, except that he is permitted to leave it for the sake of his right and as a concession. Since he is allowed to take the concession regarding what pertains to his bodily interests, then regarding what pertains to his religious interests (fulfilling his debt) is more appropriate, and his act being a repealer of other (fasts) depends on his turning away from the concession and adhering to the resolve. If he does not do so, it remains...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage introduces the second type of time-bound obligations, where time serves as both a measure (mi'yar) and a cause (sabab) for the obligation, exemplified by the month of Ramadan for fasting. The ruling is that once the time is established, other acts (like voluntary fasting) are negated because the measure is filled by the obligation. An analogy is drawn with measured and weighed goods: the measure is exclusive.
A dispute arises regarding the traveler: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that since Ramadan fasting is legislated for all, including the traveler, but the traveler is allowed to leave it, he cannot substitute it with another fast (e.g., making up a missed fast). His intention to fast something else is ineffective because no other fast is legislated during Ramadan. This applies also if he intends a voluntary fast or has an absolute intention. The same rule applies to the sick person.
Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the obligation of Ramadan is binding on the traveler; his performance of the Ramadan fast is valid, but he is given a concession to not fast. Since he is permitted to take concessions for bodily needs, it is more appropriate to allow him to fulfill his religious duty (making up a missed fast). Therefore, if he intends to fast for a missed Ramadan, it is valid, and his act serves as a repealer of the other obligation only if he consciously chooses the resolve (azima) over the concession.

Key Terms
المعيَّار (al-mi'yar): A measure or standard by which the obligation is quantified and known; in this case, the month of Ramadan is the measure for fasting.
السبب (al-sabab): A cause that triggers the obligation; witnessing part of the month of Ramadan is the cause for the obligation of fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a traveler's fast for a missed Ramadan valid during Ramadan?
A) Because the traveler is not obligated to fast Ramadan
B) Because the obligation is binding on him and he may choose the resolve over the concession
C) Because the time is a container and not a cause
D) Because the Sahibayn agree with him

Key Takeaway
When time serves both as measure and cause for an obligation, it generally excludes other acts; however, the Hanafi school differs on whether a traveler can substitute another obligation during that time, with Abu Hanifa allowing it based on the traveler's choice of resolve over concession.

Time as Standard vs Cause in Hanafi Usul
Parsing the roles of time in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether time is a cause (sabab) or a standard (miyar) for a given act of worship and derive the corresponding ruling on expiation and validity.

Core Idea
Time in worship is a standard, not a cause; missing it requires no expiation.

In Hanafi usul, the role of time in acts of worship is not uniform. This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul introduces the critical distinction between time as a cause (sabab) that triggers obligations and time as a standard (miyar) that merely measures the act. Understanding this distinction clarifies rulings on voluntary fasting, vowed fasting, expiations, and even Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two roles of time
The passage distinguishes between time as a cause (sabab) and time as a standard (miyar). When time is a cause, missing it may entail compensation; when it is a standard, no compensation.
The phrase 'فالوقت فيها معيار لا سبب' is the key textual evidence.
2
Apply to voluntary fasting
Voluntary fasting is measured by the whole day; it is invalidated by any contravention at any point and cannot be performed by intention at the end.
The author uses the term 'مقدر بكل اليوم' to show time as a standard.
3
Analyze vowed fasting
A vowed fast on a specific time becomes obligatory, but if one fasts for another obligation (e.g., expiation), it is valid due to the vow's limited authority over the individual's right, not over the Lawgiver's right.
The distinction between the right of the servant and the right of the Lawgiver is crucial.
4
Distinguish non-specific expiations
For expiations like making up Ramadan or absolute vows, time is a standard; thus intention at the start is necessary and there is no lapse (fawat).
The passage states: 'لا فوات له لما لم يكن الوقت متعيناً'.
5
Examine the problematic case of Hajj
The passage ends with a question: is Hajj's time the entire lifetime (so time is a standard) or the specific months of the first year (so time is a cause)? This remains unresolved in this text.
This is termed 'المشكل' (problematic) because the role of time is ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الوجود راجح، وبطل الترجيح بصفة العبادة؛ لأنه حال بعد الوجود، والكثرة والقلة من باب الوجود، والوجود قبل الحال، فوجب الترجيح به، على ما يأتي بيانه في باب الترجيح إن شاء الله تعالى. ولأن صيانة الوقت الذي لا درك له أصلاً على العباد واجبة، وهو مع النقصان معنى قول مشايخنا رحمهم الله: إن أداء العبادة في وقتها أولى، فصار هذا الترجيح متعارضاً، وهذا الوجه يوجب أن لا كفارة فيه، ويُروى ذلك عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه. ولم نقل بالاستناد، ولا بفساد الجزء الأول مع احتمال طريق الصحة. والإمساك في أول النهار قربة مع قصور معنى الطاعة فيه؛ لأنه لا مشقة في الإمساك في أول النهار، فصار إثبات العزيمة فيه تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً؛ وفاء لحقه، وتوفيراً لحظه. وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا: إن صوم النفل مقدر بكل اليوم، حتى فسد بوجود المنافي في أوله ولم يتأد إلا من أوله، ولم يتأد بالنية في الآخر؛ لأن الصوم عرف قربة بمعياره، ولم يعرف معياره إلا بيوم كامل، فلم يجز شرع العبادة بالرأي. وأما الإمساك في أول يوم النحر، فلم يشرع صوماً، ولكن ليكون ابتداء التناول من القرابين؛ كراهية للأضياف قبل طعامها. ومن هذا الجنس الصوم المنذور في وقت بعينه: لما انقلب بالنذر صوم الوقت واجباً لم يبق نفلاً؛ لأنه واحد لا يقبل وصفين متضادين، فصار واحداً من هذا الوجه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم. ومع الخطأ في الوصف، وتوقف مطلق الإمساك فيه على صوم الوقت، وهو المنذور، لكنه إذا صامه عن كفارة أو قضاء ما عليه: صح عما نوى؛ لأن التعيين حصل بولاية الناذر وولايته لا تعدوه، فصح التعيين فيما يرجع إلى حقه، وهو أن لا يبقى النفل مشروعاً. فأما فيما يرجع إلى حق صاحب الشرع، وهو أن لا يبقى الوقت محتملاً لحقه: فلا فاعتبر في احتمال ذلك العارض بما لو لم ينذر. وأما الوقت الذي جعل معياراً، لا سبباً فمثل الكفارات المؤقتة بأوقات غير متعينة، كقضاء رمضان، والنذر المطلق، والوقت فيها معيار، لا سبب. ومن حكمها: أنها من حيث جعلت قربة: لا تستغني عن النية، وذلك في أكثر الإمساك، ومن حيث إنها غير متعينة: لا يتوقف الإمساك فيها إلا على صوم الوقت، وهو النفل، فأما على الواجب: فلا؛ لأنه محتمل الوقت. وإنما التوقف على الموضوعات الأصلية، فأما على المحتمل: فلا، فلذلك كانت النية من أوله شرطاً؛ ليقع الإمساك من أوله من العارض الذي يحتمله الوقت. فأما إذا توقف على وجه فلا يحتمل الانتقال إلى غيره. ومن حكمه: أنه لا فوات له لما لم يكن الوقت متعيناً. وأما النوع الرابع من المؤقتة فهو المشكل منه وهو حج الإسلام، ومعنى قولنا إنه مشكل: أن وقته العمر، وأشهر الحج في كل عام صالح لأدائه، أم أشهر الحج من العام الأول وقت متعين لأدائه؟
In existence it is preponderant, and preponderance by the quality of worship is invalid because it is a state after existence. Abundance and scarcity fall under existence, and existence precedes the state, so preponderance by it is necessary, as will be explained in the chapter on preponderance, God willing. And because preserving time, which has absolutely no compensation, is obligatory upon the servants. And this, with deficiency, is the meaning of our scholars' statement: 'Performing worship in its time is better.' So this preponderance becomes conflicting, and this aspect necessitates that there is no expiation in it, and that is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God be pleased with him. We do not adopt retroactive effectiveness nor the invalidity of the first part with the possibility of validity. And refraining at the beginning of the day is a devotional act despite the deficiency of the meaning of obedience in it because there is no hardship in refraining at the beginning of the day. So affirming determination in it is by estimation, not by realization; in fulfillment of its right and to maximize its share. Upon this principle we said: Voluntary fasting is measured by the entire day, such that it is invalidated by the existence of a contravention at its beginning and is only performed from its beginning, and is not performed by the intention at the end because fasting is known as a devotional act by its standard, and its standard is not known except by a complete day. So it is not permissible to legislate worship by opinion. As for refraining on the first day of Sacrifice, it was not legislated as fasting, but rather so that the beginning of eating is from the sacrificial animals, out of dislike for the guests before their food. From this category is vowed fasting at a specific time: when the time's fast becomes obligatory due to the vow, it does not remain voluntary because it is one thing that does not accept two contradictory descriptions. So it becomes one from this aspect, and it is affected by the absolute name. And with the error in the description, the absolute refraining in it depends on the fast of the time, which is the vowed one. But if he fasts it for an expiation or a makeup of what is owed, it is valid for what he intended because specification occurred by the authority of the one who vowed, and his authority does not go beyond it. So the specification is valid regarding what pertains to his right, which is that the voluntary does not remain legislated. As for what pertains to the right of the Lawgiver, which is that the time does not remain probable for His right, it is not, so consideration is given to that probable contingent as if he had not vowed. As for time that is made a standard, not a cause, such as expiations that are time-bound with non-specific times, like making up Ramadan and the absolute vow, time in them is a standard, not a cause. Among its rulings: that insofar as they are made devotional, they are not free from intention, and that is in most of the refraining. And insofar as they are non-specific, refraining in them depends only on the fast of the time, which is voluntary. As for the obligatory, it does not, because the time is probable. Rather, dependence is on original subjects, not on what is probable. Therefore, intention at its beginning is a condition so that refraining occurs from its beginning due to the contingent that the time bears. As for if it depends on something, it does not admit transfer to another. Among its rulings: there is no lapse because the time is not specified. The fourth type of time-bound acts is the problematic one, which is the Hajj of Islam. The meaning of our saying it is problematic: its time is life, and the months of Hajj in every year are suitable for performing it, or are the months of Hajj from the first year a specified time for performing it?
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the principle that time in acts of worship is treated as a standard (miyār) rather than a cause (sabab), and it applies this to several cases. The author begins by stating a preponderance rule: in existence, preponderance is by the act's existence, not by its quality. He then introduces the concept that preserving time is obligatory on the servants because time once lost cannot be recovered. This leads to the conclusion that performing worship in its time is better, even if the act is deficient. This principle creates a conflict in the earlier preponderance, and as a result, no expiation (kaffāra) is required for missing the time—a view narrated from Abu Hanifa. The author rejects the ideas of retroactive effect (istinād) and nullification of the first part if a later part is valid. Next, he explains that refraining (imṣāk) at the beginning of the day in voluntary fasting is considered a devotional act despite the lack of hardship, so the determination of the act is by estimation rather than realization. He then applies this principle to voluntary fasting: it is measured by the whole day, so it is invalidated by a contravention at any point and cannot be performed by intention at the end. He then addresses the first day of Eid al-Adha, where refraining from eating before the sacrifice is not a fast but a preparatory act. Vowed fasting on a specific time becomes obligatory by the vow; if one fasts for a different obligation like expiation, it is valid because the vow's authority is limited to the individual's right, but it does not override the Lawgiver's right to the time. Finally, the author distinguishes between time as a standard (like in non-specific expiations and makeup fasts) and time as a cause. For time-as-standard acts, intention at the start is necessary because the time is probable. The passage concludes with the fourth type of time-bound act: Hajj, which is problematic because its time could be lifetime or the specific months of the first year.

Key Terms
مؤقتة (muwaqqata): Time-bound acts of worship; acts whose performance is tied to a specific time.
معيار (miyār): A standard or measure; time that serves only as a gauge for the act, not as a cause for it.
سبب (sabab): A cause that triggers the obligation or validity of an act.
لا درك له (lā daraka lahu): It has no compensation; time once lost cannot be made up or compensated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on expiation (kaffāra) when someone delays an act of worship from its optimal time?
A) Expiation is required.
B) No expiation is required.
C) Expiation is required only if the delay was intentional.
D) It depends on the type of worship.

Key Takeaway
Time in Hanafi usul is primarily a standard (miyar) for worship, not a cause (sabab); thus missing it does not incur expiation unless specified.

The Time of Hajj Obligation: Immediacy or Flexibility?
Analysing the time of Hajj obligation and voluntary Hajj validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the immediacy of Hajj obligation and apply the principle that time is a vessel (zarf) not a measure (miyar) to determine the validity of voluntary Hajj alongside the obligatory.

Core Idea
The time for Hajj is a vessel, not a measure; delay is permissible and voluntary Hajj is valid even before the obligatory one.

This passage tackles a profound usul question: does the command to perform Hajj obligate immediate performance in the first possible season, or is there flexibility? The Hanafi school is divided, with Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holding that the first year is not exclusively determined, while his senior Abu Yusuf argues for immediacy. The debate hinges on the nature of time in worship: is it a container or a measure? Understanding this distinction clarifies when voluntary Hajj is valid and when delaying becomes sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
What is the exact point of disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf? Is it about the binding nature of the first possible Hajj season, or something else?
Focus on the term 'muta'ayyin' (determined) and how it applies to the first year.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's argument
He argues that the first year is not automatically determined. His proof: voluntary Hajj is valid in that same year. If it were determined, voluntary would be invalid, like fasting on Ramadan days.
Also note the analogy with make-up fasts (qada) where any day is valid.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's counterargument
He likens the first Hajj season to the time of Zuhr prayer: it is exclusive and cannot be delayed. His key point: competition for another time is based on doubtful future life, so the present season remains exclusive.
Consider his use of the rare death scenario to show that the apparent (life) is not abandoned for the rare.
4
Understand the Hanafi resolution
The text supports Imam Muhammad by affirming the principle that time is a vessel (zarf) not a measure (miyar). The ruling: voluntary Hajj is valid even for one who owes the obligatory Hajj.
This also implies that delaying the obligatory Hajj to a later year is not sinful, according to Imam Muhammad.
5
Compare with al-Shafi'i's position
Al-Shafi'i disallows voluntary Hajj before the obligatory, treating it as disrespectful. The Hanafi response dismisses this as similar to restraining a foolish person, implying it is an overreach.
Note the different usul principles: Hanafi reliance on the vessel concept vs. Shafi'i's reverence (ta'dhim) for the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوجب الفور بلا خلاف.
ذلك محمد فمسألة مبتدأة: فذهب في [رحمه الله] فأما مسألة الحج إلى أن الحج فرض العمر بلا خلاف، إلا أنه لا يُتأدى في كل عام إلا في وقت خاص، فيكون وقته نوعاً من أنواع أشهر الحج في عمره، وإليه تعيينه، كصوم القضاء وقته النُّهَرُ، دون الليالي، وإلى العبد تعيينه، فلا يتعين الذي يليه إلا بتعيينه بطريق الأداء.
ألا ترى أنه متى أداه كان مؤدياً، ولو كان الأول متعيناً لصار بالتأخير مفوتاً.
والدليل عليه : أنه بقي وقتاً للنفل، مع أنه لم يُشرع في مدة واحدة إلا حج واحد، ولو تعين للفرض: لما بقي النفل مشروعاً، كما في شهر رمضان، فثبت أنه غير متعيّن إلا بالأداء، ومتى تعين بالأداء: لم يبق النفل فيه مشروعاً.
ولأبي يوسف رحمه الله : أن أشهر الحج من العام الأول متعيّنةٌ للأداء، فلا يحل له التأخير عنها، كوقت الظهر للظهر.
وإنما قلنا هذا؛ لأن الخطاب بالأداء لحقه في هذا الوقت، وهو واحدٌ لا مزاحِمَ له؛ لأن المزاحمة لا تثبت إلا بإدراك وقت آخر، وهو مشكوك ؛ لأنه لا يدركه إلا بالحياة، والحياة والممات في هذه المدة سواء في الاحتمال، فلا يثبت الإدراك بالشك، فبقي هذا الوقت متعيّناً بلا معارضة.
ويصير الساقط بطريق التعارض كالساقط بالحقيقة، فيصير كوقت الظهر في التقدير، بخلاف صوم القضاء؛ لأن تأخيره عن اليوم الأول لا يفوته، والتعارض للحال غير قائم؛ لأن الحياة إلى اليوم الثاني غالبةٌ، والموت في ليلة واحدة بالفُجاءة نادر، فلا يُترك الظاهر بالنادر.
وإذا كان كذلك استوت الأيام كلّها كأنه أدركها جملةً، فخير بينها، ولم يتعين أولها.
ولا يلزم أن النفل بقي مشروعاً ؛ لأنا إنما اعتبرنا التعيين احتياطاً، واحترازاً عن الفوات، فظهر ذلك في حق المأثم، لا غير، فأما أن يبطل اختيار جهة التقصير والمأثم بالشروع في النفل : فلا .
ولا يلزم إذا أدرك العام الثاني ؛ لأنا إنما عيَّنا الأول لوقوع الشك، فإذا أدركه، وذهب الشك: صار الثاني هو المتعين، وسقط الماضي؛ لأن الماضي لا يحتمل الأداء بعد مضيه، وفي إدراك الثالث: شك، فقام الثاني مقام الأول. ومن حكم هذا الأصل أن وقت الحج ظرف له، لا معيار، ألا ترى أنه يفضل عن أدائه، وأن الحج أفعال عُرفت بأسمائها وصفاتها، لا بمعيارها، فأشبه وقت الظهر، فلا يَدفعُ غيره من جنسه.
ولهذا قلنا: إن التطوع بالحج يصح ممن عليه حجة الإسلام، كالنفل ممن عليه الظهر.
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما عَظُم أمرُ الحج : استحسنًا في الحَجْر عن التطوع ؛ صيانة له، وإشفاقاً عليه.
وهو نظيرُ حَجْر السفيه، فإن هذا سَفَه. من هذا ومثل هذا مشروع، فإنه صح بإطلاق النية، وصح أصله بلا نية ممن
It necessitates immediate performance without dispute. That is Muhammad, so a new issue: he went, may Allah have mercy on him, as for the issue of Hajj: that Hajj is a lifetime obligation without dispute, except that it is not performed every year except at a specific time. Thus its time is a type of the months of Hajj in his lifetime, and its determination is up to him, like the fast of make-up: its time is the daytime, not the nights, and its determination is up to the servant, so the one that follows is not determined except by his determination through performance. Do you not see that whenever he performs it, he is a performer, and if the first were determined, it would have become lost by delay. The proof for it: that it remains a time for voluntary (Hajj), even though only one Hajj is prescribed in a single period, and if it were determined for the obligatory, the voluntary would not remain prescribed, as in the month of Ramadan. Thus it is established that it is not determined except by performance, and when it is determined by performance, the voluntary does not remain prescribed in it. Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, holds: the months of Hajj of the first year are specifically for performance, so he may not delay them, like the time of Zuhr for Zuhr. And we only say this because the address to perform is attached to him in this time, and it is one with no competitor, because competition is only established by reaching another time, and that is doubtful, because he only reaches it by life, and life and death in this period are equal in probability, so reaching is not established by doubt, thus this time remains determined without opposition. And what is dropped by way of opposition becomes like what is dropped in reality, so it becomes like the time of Zuhr in estimation, unlike the fast of make-up, because delaying it past the first day does not cause it to be lost, and the opposition for the present is not established, because life until the second day is predominant, and death in a single night suddenly is rare, so the apparent is not abandoned for the rare. And if that is so, all the days become equal as if he reached them all at once, so he is given choice between them, and its first is not determined. And it does not follow that the voluntary remains prescribed, because we considered determination only as a precaution and to avoid loss, so that appears with regard to sin only, not otherwise. As for invalidating the choice of the direction of shortcoming and sin by starting voluntary: no. And it does not follow if he reaches the second year, because we determined the first only due to doubt, so when he reaches it and the doubt goes away, the second becomes determined, and the past drops, because the past cannot support performance after its passing, and in reaching the third there is doubt, so the second stands in place of the first. And from the ruling of this principle is that the time of Hajj is a vessel for it, not a measure, do you not see that it can exceed its performance, and that Hajj is actions known by their names and attributes, not by their measure, so it resembles the time of Zuhr, so it does not repel another of its kind. For this we say: voluntary Hajj is valid from one who owes the Hajj of Islam, like voluntary prayer from one who owes Zuhr. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: since the matter of Hajj is great, they considered it good to prevent voluntary (Hajj) to protect it and out of compassion for it. And it is similar to restraining a foolish person, for this is foolishness. From this and like this are prescribed, for it is valid with absolute intention, and its origin is valid without intention from one who...
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the time for performing the obligatory Hajj and whether the command implies immediate performance in the first possible season. The author presents the view of Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that Hajj is a lifetime obligation, but its time is not automatically the first year; rather, the individual may choose to perform it in any year of their life, since the time is a vessel (zarf) and not a measure (miyar). The proof given is that if the first year were determined, voluntary Hajj would not be valid in that same year, yet it is known that voluntary Hajj is allowed. Abu Yusuf argues that the months of the first year are specifically for performance, analogous to the time of Zuhr prayer, and delaying would be impermissible. The Hanafi response (from Imam Muhammad's perspective) refutes this by pointing out that competition for the time only arises if another time is definitely reached, which is doubtful due to the possibility of death; thus the first year remains determined but only by performance, not by the command itself. The text then compares this to make-up fasts, where the first day is not exclusive because life is predominant and delay is possible without loss. The conclusion is that voluntary Hajj is valid even for one who owes the obligatory Hajj, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, who forbids it out of reverence. The author dismisses Shafi'i's stance as akin to restraining a foolish person, implying it is an overreach.

Key Terms
فرض العمر (fard al-‘umr): An obligation that must be performed once in a lifetime, like Hajj.
متعين (muta‘ayyin): Determined or specified for a particular time, making other times not equivalent.
تطوع (tatawwu‘): Voluntary, supererogatory worship.
حجة الإسلام (hijjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj that every Muslim must perform once in a lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's view presented in this passage, is a voluntary Hajj valid for someone who has not yet performed the obligatory Hajj?
A) Yes, because voluntary Hajj is always valid regardless of obligation.
B) No, because the obligatory Hajj must be done first before any voluntary Hajj.
C) Yes, because the time of Hajj is a vessel not a measure, and voluntary acts are prescribed alongside obligations.
D) No, because the first year is exclusively for the obligatory Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The time for Hajj is a vessel, not a measure; thus, delaying obligatory Hajj is not sinful, and voluntary Hajj is valid even before the obligatory one, in the Hanafi view of Imam Muhammad.

Time as Container: The Hanafi Principle for Hajj
Establishing the usul principle that time for Hajj is a container (zarf) not a measure (mi'yar), with a qiyas to Zuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that time for Hajj is a container (zarf) not a measure (mi'yar) to derive the ruling that voluntary Hajj is valid despite an outstanding obligatory Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj time is a container, not a measure – multiple Hajj acts in one season do not exclude one another.

In this passage, al-Bazdawi establishes a core usul principle that distinguishes the time of Hajj from the time of prayer. While prayer times are measured (mi'yar), the time of Hajj is merely a container (zarf) for the actions. Since the actions of Hajj are defined by their names and descriptions, not by a temporal measure, multiple performances within the same time are possible. This principle directly leads to the Hanafi ruling that a person who owes the obligatory Hajj may validly perform a voluntary Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish zarf from mi'yar
Understand the difference between time as a container (zarf) and time as a measure (mi'yar). The time of Hajj is a container because the actions are known by their names and descriptions, not by a specific temporal window.
Contrast with prayer times which are measures (e.g., Zuhr time is defined by the sun's position).
2
Apply the qiyas with Zuhr
The time of Hajj resembles the time of Zuhr, which is also a container. In Zuhr time, one can perform multiple prayers (e.g., obligatory and voluntary) without one pushing away the other.
The qiyas is based on the shared illa: both are containers for acts defined by their own descriptions.
3
Derive the Hanafi ruling
From the principle and qiyas, conclude that a voluntary Hajj is valid even if one owes the obligatory Hajj, just as voluntary prayers are valid alongside the obligatory Zuhr.
This ruling is the direct outcome of the usul principle.

Source Text

And ihram according to us is a condition like wudu, so it is valid by the action of another, by indication of the command. As for actions, they must occur from his body. And its permissibility when absolute is by indication of determination from the performer, for the apparent is that he does not intend voluntary while he owes the Hajj of Islam, so the determination becomes due to a meaning in the performer, not in the performed. So if he intends voluntary, he has come with an explicit statement contrary to it, so it is invalidated. And contrary to the month of Ramadan, because it is determined with no competitor in its time, not due to a meaning in the performer. And this is like the currency of the country: when it is determined due to a meaning in the performer (which is ease of attaining it) as a divine indication, it becomes invalid when explicitly stating other than it. As for the unrestricted with respect to time, it is with deferment as we have indicated, and Allah knows best. Contrary to al-Karkhi, may Allah have mercy on him. And from this principle: the chapter of prohibition.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul establishes a key principle: the time for Hajj is a container (zarf) for the act, not a measure (mi'yar) by which the act is judged. This is unlike prayer times which are measured (e.g., Zuhr has a specific window). The author argues that since Hajj actions are defined by their names and descriptions (e.g., standing at Arafat, circumambulation), and not by a temporal measure, it resembles the time for Zuhr (which is a container but also has a measure? Actually, Zuhr time is a container but there's a specific measure; the author means that like Zuhr, the time of Hajj can accommodate multiple performances without invalidating one another). From this principle, he derives a ruling: it is valid for a person who owes the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam) to perform a voluntary Hajj in the same year, just as it is valid for one who owes the Zuhr prayer to perform voluntary prayers before or after. This is the Hanafi position. The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection: because Hajj is great, it is better to prevent voluntary Hajj to protect the obligatory one, analogous to preventing a foolish person from squandering wealth. The Hanafi response: such prevention would eliminate choice (ikhtiyar), which is essential for worship. Worship is never valid without choice. The choice here is the performer's intention. Moreover, ihram (the state of consecration) is a condition like wudu, which can be performed by another (e.g., one can make ihram for an unconscious person). However, the actions themselves must be performed by the one who owes the obligation. When someone owes Hajjat al-Islam and performs Hajj without specifying (mutlaq), it is assumed to be for the obligatory, because the default is that he intends the obligatory. If he explicitly intends voluntary (nafl), his explicit intention overrides the default and invalidates the presumption, making the Hajj valid only as voluntary? Actually the text says 'فبطل به' meaning the specification for obligatory is invalidated, so the Hajj becomes voluntary? The text is somewhat ambiguous; it likely means the Hajj is invalid for the obligatory but valid as voluntary? However, the Hanafi position is that the voluntary is valid even if intended, but the obligatory remains owed. The text contrasts with Ramadan, where fasting is specifically determined (mut'ayyan) with no competing act, so one cannot intend nafl instead. Similarly, like the currency of a country: if one is required to pay in local currency, specifying another currency invalidates the payment. Finally, the author notes that for unrestricted obligations (like Hajj not tied to a specific time), the binding is with deferment (ala al-tarakhi), contrary to al-Karkhi who held it is immediate.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A container or vessel; here referring to time as a receptacle for an act, not a standard by which the act is measured.
معيار (mi'yar): A measure or standard; here referring to time as a criterion that determines the validity or count of an act.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship; supererogatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed in this lesson, what is the relationship between the time of Hajj and the performance of multiple Hajj acts?
A) The time is a measure, so it can only contain one valid Hajj.
B) The time is a container, so it can accommodate multiple performances.
C) The time is a container, but only for the obligatory Hajj.
D) The time is a measure, but voluntary is allowed if preceded by obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The time for Hajj is a container, not a measure, which allows the coexistence of voluntary and obligatory Hajj in the same season.

Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute: Voluntary Hajj During Obligatory Duty
Presenting the Shafi'i objection to voluntary Hajj and the Hanafi rebuttal, with additional supporting arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i arguments regarding the validity of voluntary Hajj when the obligatory Hajj is owed, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Blocking voluntary Hajj to protect the obligatory eliminates choice, which is essential for worship – a crucial Hanafi objection to the Shafi'i position.

This passage presents the Shafi'i argument that because Hajj is great, voluntary acts should be prevented to safeguard the obligatory, similar to preventing a foolish person from wasting wealth. The Hanafi response is that such prevention eliminates the free choice (ikhtiyar) without which worship is invalid. This dispute highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the performer's intention and the nature of ihram as a condition. The lesson also covers the role of default intention (ta'yin) and how explicit intention overrides it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i objection
Recall that Hanafi rules voluntary Hajj valid; Shafi'i objects by analogy with blocking a foolish person.
The Shafi'i view is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to protect the greatness of Hajj.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i analogy
The Shafi'i compares the one who performs voluntary Hajj while owing the obligatory to a foolish person who squanders wealth – the state should block him.
This analogy suggests that voluntary Hajj is a form of waste because the obligation is not yet fulfilled.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal on choice
Hanafi argues that blocking voluntary Hajj would eliminate the performer's choice, and worship is not valid without choice (ikhtiyar).
Choice is fundamental; the Hanafi position preserves the individual's free will in devotion.
4
Consider additional Hanafi arguments
Hanafi adds that ihram is a condition like wudu, which can be performed by another, but actions must be performed by the subject. Also, default intention (ta'yin) favors the obligation unless explicitly stated otherwise.
These strengthen the Hanafi position and show the depth of the proof.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi, the voluntary Hajj is valid and the obligatory remains owed; in Shafi'i, the voluntary is invalid, and the person must repeat the Hajj (if he did it) to fulfill the obligation.
This shows the real-world impact of this usul dispute.

And something like this is prescribed, for it is valid with absolute intention, and its origin is valid without intention from one whose companions perform ihram on his behalf during his unconsciousness, and by a man's ihram on behalf of his parents. But we say: prohibition in this eliminates choice, and this contradicts worship, and worship is never valid without choice, but choice in every chapter is appropriate to it. And ihram according to us is a condition like wudu, so it is valid by the action of another, by indication of the command. As for actions, they must occur from his body. And its permissibility when absolute is by indication of determination from the performer, for the apparent is that he does not intend voluntary while he owes the Hajj of Islam, so the determination becomes due to a meaning in the performer, not in the performed. So if he intends voluntary, he has come with an explicit statement contrary to it, so it is invalidated. And contrary to the month of Ramadan, because it is determined with no competitor in its time, not due to a meaning in the performer. And this is like the currency of the country: when it is determined due to a meaning in the performer (which is ease of attaining it) as a divine indication, it becomes invalid when explicitly stating other than it. As for the unrestricted with respect to time, it is with deferment as we have indicated, and Allah knows best. Contrary to al-Karkhi, may Allah have mercy on him. And from this principle: the chapter of prohibition.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul establishes a key principle: the time for Hajj is a container (zarf) for the act, not a measure (mi'yar) by which the act is judged. This is unlike prayer times which are measured (e.g., Zuhr has a specific window). The author argues that since Hajj actions are defined by their names and descriptions (e.g., standing at Arafat, circumambulation), and not by a temporal measure, it resembles the time for Zuhr (which is a container but also has a measure? Actually, Zuhr time is a container but there's a specific measure; the author means that like Zuhr, the time of Hajj can accommodate multiple performances without invalidating one another). From this principle, he derives a ruling: it is valid for a person who owes the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam) to perform a voluntary Hajj in the same year, just as it is valid for one who owes the Zuhr prayer to perform voluntary prayers before or after. This is the Hanafi position. The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection: because Hajj is great, it is better to prevent voluntary Hajj to protect the obligatory one, analogous to preventing a foolish person from squandering wealth. The Hanafi response: such prevention would eliminate choice (ikhtiyar), which is essential for worship. Worship is never valid without choice. The choice here is the performer's intention. Moreover, ihram (the state of consecration) is a condition like wudu, which can be performed by another (e.g., one can make ihram for an unconscious person). However, the actions themselves must be performed by the one who owes the obligation. When someone owes Hajjat al-Islam and performs Hajj without specifying (mutlaq), it is assumed to be for the obligatory, because the default is that he intends the obligatory. If he explicitly intends voluntary (nafl), his explicit intention overrides the default and invalidates the presumption, making the Hajj valid only as voluntary? Actually the text says 'فبطل به' meaning the specification for obligatory is invalidated, so the Hajj becomes voluntary? The text is somewhat ambiguous; it likely means the Hajj is invalid for the obligatory but valid as voluntary? However, the Hanafi position is that the voluntary is valid even if intended, but the obligatory remains owed. The text contrasts with Ramadan, where fasting is specifically determined (mut'ayyan) with no competing act, so one cannot intend nafl instead. Similarly, like the currency of a country: if one is required to pay in local currency, specifying another currency invalidates the payment. Finally, the author notes that for unrestricted obligations (like Hajj not tied to a specific time), the binding is with deferment (ala al-tarakhi), contrary to al-Karkhi who held it is immediate.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification or determination; here referring to the default assumption that a general performance is for the obligatory duty unless explicitly intended otherwise.
اختيار (ikhtiyar): Free choice; the conscious decision to perform an act of worship.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning where a ruling is preferred over qiyas due to considerations of public interest, necessity, or ease.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by specific clothing and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, what is the default ruling if a person who owes Hajjat al-Islam performs Hajj without specifying intention?
A) The Hajj counts for the obligatory Hajj.
B) The Hajj counts as voluntary, and the obligatory remains.
C) The Hajj is invalid.
D) The Hajj is void unless explicitly intended for the obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits voluntary Hajj despite the obligatory duty, emphasizing the performer's choice and intention, while the Shafi'i school prohibits it out of caution for the greatness of Hajj.

Effect of Prohibition on Validity: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Usul dispute on prohibition and validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the effect of prohibition on validity, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and apply the principle to new cases.

Core Idea
Prohibition (nahy) attaches as an attribute without destroying the essence: the act remains valid but forbidden.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Bazdawi tackles a foundational debate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does a prohibition (nahy) automatically nullify the act, or can the act remain valid while being forbidden? The Hanafi school argues that the two can coexist, supported by numerous examples from the Shari'ah. Understanding this principle is essential for deriving rulings on many practical matters, from prayer in usurped land to divorce during menstruation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi claim: prohibition does not invalidate the act; the act is valid in essence but carries the attribute of being prohibited (qabih).
This is the core thesis.
2
Identify the opposing school's argument
State the Shafi'i position: prohibition necessarily invalidates the act because legitimacy comes from command, and prohibition contradicts that.
The text calls this 'utmost contradiction and corruption'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi logical proof
Follow the Hanafi reasoning: if prohibition nullified the act, the attribute would destroy the essence; but they are distinct, so the essence remains. The prohibition is subsidiary (follows the act), not primary.
Key distinction: essence vs. attribute.
4
Examine the empirical evidence from Shari'ah
Review the examples given: invalid ihram, forbidden divorce, prayer in usurped land, fasting on day of doubt. In each case, the act is legally effective despite being prohibited.
These demonstrate that legal acts can 'bear' the attribute of prohibition.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: e.g., prayer in usurped land. Hanafi: valid (obligation fulfilled) but sinful; Shafi'i: invalid and must be repeated.
This affects a mufti's fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القُبح : فوصف قائم بالمنهي عنه)، مقتضى به؛ تحقيقاً لحكمه فكان ،تابعاً فلا يجوز تحقيقه على وجه يبطل به ما أوجبه واقتضاه، فيصير المقتضى دليلاً على الفساد بعد أن كان دليلاً على الصحة. بل يجب العمل بالأصل في موضعه، والعمل بالمقتضى بقدر الإمكان، وهو أن يُجعل القبحُ وصفاً للمشروع، فيصير مشروعاً بأصله، غير مشروع بوصفه، فيصير فاسداً. هذا غاية تحقيق هذا الأصل. فأما الشافعي رحمه الله ، فقد حقق المقتضى، وأبطل المقتضي، وهذا في غاية المناقضة والفساد. * فإن قيل: هذا صحيح في الأفعال الحسية؛ لأنها لا تنعدم بصفة القبح، فأما الشرعية فتنعدم ؛ لما قلنا فلا بدَّ من إقامة الدلالة على أن المشروعات تحتمل هذا الوصف. قيل له: قد وجدنا المشروع يحتمل الفساد بالنهي، كالإحرام الفاسد والطلاق الحرام والصلاة الحرام (۲) ، والصوم المحظور في الشك (١) ، وما أشبه ذلك، فوجب إثباته على هذا الوجه؛ رعاية لمنازل المشروعات، ومحافظة لحدودها، وعلى هذا الأصل تُخرج الفروع كلها. و قال: «ثلاث ساعات كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهانا أن نصلي فيهن، وأن نقبر فيهن موتانا : حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع، وحين يقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تزول، وحين تَضيَّفُ الشمس للغروب حتى تغرب». رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري، واللفظ لمسلم. قال : والمواطن السبعة أخرج ابن ماجه والترمذي من طريق زيد بن جبيرة عن ابن عمر «أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى أن يُصلَّى في سبعة مواطن: في المزبلة والمجزرة والمقبرة، وقارعة الطريق وفي الحمام، وفي معاطن الإبل، وفوق بيت الله تعالى». قال الترمذي : ليس إسناده بذاك القوي، وقد تكلّم في زيد بن جبيرة من قِبَل حفظه. قلت : قد قالوا: إن الحرام ما كان بقطعي، فكيف أطلق هنا، ولا قاطع؟! (۱) قوله : والصوم المحظور يوم الشك : عن صلة بن زفر قال: كنا عند عمار بن ياسر في اليوم الذي يُشَكُّ فيه، فأُتي بشاة مَصْليَّة، فتنحى بعض القوم، فقال عمار: من صام هذا اليوم فقد عصا أبا القاسم». رواه الخمسة، وصححه ابن خزيمة وابن حبان، وأخرج الخطيب في تاريخ بغداد عن ابن عباس قال: «مَن صام اليوم الذي يُشك فيه: فقد عصى الله ورسوله»، وذَكَرَ له متابعاً. ووقع في «الهداية» بلفظ : « لا يُصام اليوم الذي يُشك فيه»، مرفوعاً، قال المخرجون لا يُعرف ولا أصل له قلتُ : بل له أصل، وهو ما روى الإمام أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه عن عبد الملك بن عمير عن قَزعة عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن صيام اليوم الذي يُشك فيه من رمضان». (۲) قوله : والصلاة الحرام: قال الشارح: هي الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة، سيأتي لي في هذا كلام قال والأوقات المكروهة فيه عن عقبة بن عامر الجهني
As for the 'ugly' (prohibition): it is an attribute subsisting in the prohibited act, necessitated by it, to actualize its ruling. Thus it is subsidiary, so it is not permissible to actualize it in a way that nullifies what it (the act) necessitates and demands. So the necessitated (prohibition) becomes evidence for invalidity after it was evidence for validity. Rather, it is necessary to act on the original (principle) in its place, and act on the necessitated (prohibition) as much as possible, which is to make the 'ugly' an attribute of the legislated act, so it becomes legislated in its essence, not legislated in its attribute, thus it becomes invalid. This is the ultimate verification of this principle. As for al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, he actualized the necessitated (prohibition) and nullified the necessitator (the act), and this is utmost contradiction and corruption. * If it is said: This is correct for physical acts because they are not annihilated by the attribute of ugliness. As for legal (acts), they are annihilated (by it) as we said, so there must be an indication that legal acts admit this attribute. It is replied: We have found that a legislated act admits invalidity through prohibition, such as invalid ihram, forbidden divorce, forbidden prayer, and prohibited fasting on the day of doubt, and the like. So it is necessary to establish it in this manner, out of observance for the ranks of legislated acts and preservation of their boundaries, and upon this principle all branches are derived. And he said: 'Three hours the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us to pray in them and to bury our dead in them: when the sun rises until it rises high, when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines towards sunset until it sets.' Narrated by all except al-Bukhari, and the wording is Muslim's. He said: And the seven places: Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi narrated from the route of Zayd ibn Jubayra from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade prayer in seven places: in the garbage dump, the slaughterhouse, the graveyard, the middle of the road, the bathhouse, the resting places of camels, and above the House of Allah (the Kaaba). Al-Tirmidhi said: Its chain is not that strong, and Zayd ibn Jubayra has been criticized regarding his memory. I said: They said that what is 'haram' is what is definitive, so how is it used here without definitive proof? (1) His saying: Fasting prohibited on the day of doubt: from Silah ibn Zufar who said: We were with 'Ammar ibn Yasir on the day of doubt, and a roasted sheep was brought, so some people moved away. 'Ammar said: Whoever fasts this day has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim. Narrated by the five, and authenticated by Ibn Khuzaymah and Ibn Hibban. Al-Khatib in Tarikh Baghdad narrated from Ibn 'Abbas: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Allah and His Messenger.' And he mentioned a follow-up for it. In al-Hidayah it is worded: 'The day of doubt is not to be fasted' as a marfu' hadith. The hadith extractors said it is unknown and has no basis. I said: Rather it has a basis, which is what Imam Abu Hanifa narrated from 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Umair from Qaza'ah from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade fasting the day of doubt in Ramadan. (2) His saying: Forbidden prayer: the commentator said it is prayer in usurped land; there will be discussion on this later, and the disliked times were mentioned from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir al-Juhani.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on the effect of prohibition (nahy) on the validity (sihhah) of an act. The Hanafi position, as articulated by al-Bazdawi, is that prohibition does not necessarily annul the act's essential validity; rather, the act remains valid in its essence (asl) but takes on the attribute (wasf) of being forbidden (qabih). Thus, the act is 'legislated in its essence, not legislated in its attribute', meaning it is legally valid but sinful. In contrast, al-Shafi'i holds that prohibition renders the act inherently invalid (fasid). The author argues that the Shafi'i view is contradictory because it prioritizes the attribute over the essence. The objection that this applies only to physical acts, not legal ones, is refuted with examples from sacred law: invalid ihram (e.g., during hajj with forbidden conditions), forbidden divorce (e.g., during menstruation), forbidden prayer (e.g., in usurped land), and prohibited fasting (e.g., on the day of doubt). These examples show that prohibited acts can still be legally effective in some sense (e.g., divorce takes effect even if forbidden). The text then cites hadith on forbidden prayer times (three hours) and places (seven places), though it notes some weakness in the latter's chain. The commentator adds remarks on the day of doubt fasting. Overall, this principle (al-asl fi al-nahy la yufsid) is foundational for deriving many fiqh rulings in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القبح (al-qabah): An attribute of ugliness or forbiddenness that attaches to an act due to prohibition, without nullifying its essential validity.
المقتضى (al-muqtada): That which is necessitated, here the prohibition as a necessary consequence of the act's nature, but it is subsidiary to the act's essence.
المشروع (al-mashru'): A legally prescribed act; the act's essence is legislated even if its attribute becomes prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle discussed in this passage, what is the effect of a prohibition (nahy) on a legally prescribed act?
A) The act becomes invalid (fasid) and must be repeated if possible.
B) The act remains valid (sahih) in its essence but is forbidden (haram) due to the attribute of prohibition.
C) The act is altogether null and void, with no legal effect.
D) The act is suspended until the prohibition is removed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes that prohibition (nahy) does not annul the essential validity of an act; the act remains sahih but haram, a principle with wide-ranging applications in fiqh.

Fasid vs Batil: Prohibition on Description Preserves the Root
Explaining that prohibition on an attribute makes an act fasid, not batil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fasid and batil in Hanafi usul by identifying whether a prohibition targets the root (asl) or a description (wasf), and apply this distinction to new cases from contracts and worship.

Core Idea
A prohibition on a description leaves the root valid; the act becomes fasid, not batil.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul lays out a foundational Hanafi distinction: when a prohibition attaches to a description (wasf) of an act rather than its essence (asl), the act remains valid in its root but becomes corrupted in its description. This yields the category of fasid (corrupt) as distinct from batil (void). We will explore this principle through several concrete examples—wine sales, riba, fasting on Eid, and prayer at sunrise—and see how it applies to Quranic testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the opening statement: 'the sale of wine is prohibited by its description...so it becomes fasid, not batil.' Grasp that the prohibition does not strike at the contract's pillars but at an attribute of the price.
The root (asl) refers to the essential elements of the act; the description (wasf) is an attached quality.
2
Distinguish Asl from Wasf in Each Example
For each example (wine sale, riba, fasting on Eid, prayer at sunrise), identify what constitutes the valid root and what is the prohibited description. The text explicitly states these for each case.
E.g., in riba: the exchange (root) is legitimate; the excess (description) is prohibited.
3
Apply the Principle to Generate the Ruling
Since the prohibition is on the description only, the act is not void (batil) but corrupt (fasid). The consequence is that the act retains some validity but is deficient.
Fasid acts may require correction or compensation, unlike batil acts which are null and void ab initio.
4
Contrast with Batil Cases
The passage contrasts with selling a dead animal or its skin: these are batil because the subject matter itself lacks legal value (not property, not mutqawwam). Here the root is defective, not just a description.
Batil: the entire act is void; no legal effect whatsoever.
5
Extract the General Usul Rule
Formulate the rule: 'Any prohibition that attaches to a description preserves the root, making the act fasid. Only when the prohibition targets the root itself does the act become batil.' This rule applies across ibadat and muamalat.
This rule is a key Hanafi divergence from Shafi'i usul, which often treats fasid and batil as synonymous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منها: أن البيع بالخمر منهي بوصفه، وهو الثمن؛ لأن الخمر مال غير متقوم، فصلح ثمناً من وجه دون وجه فصار فاسداً، لا باطلاً، ولا خلل في ركن العقد، ولا في محله: فصار قبيحاً بوصفه، مشروعاً بأصله. وكذلك إذا اشترى خمراً بعبد؛ لأن كل واحد منهما ثمن لصاحبه، فلم ينعقد في الخمر؛ لعدم محله وانعقد في العبد؛ لوجود محله، وفسد بفساد ثمنه. بخلاف الميتة؛ لأنها ليست بمال ولا بمتقومة، فوقع البيع بلا ثمن وهو غير مشروع. وكذلك جلد الميتة؛ لأنه ليس بمال ولا بمتقوم. وكذلك بيع الربا مشروع بأصله، وهو وجود ركنه في محله، غير مشروع بوصفه، وهو الفضل في العوض، فصار فاسداً، لا باطلاً. وكذلك الشرط الفاسد في البيع: مثل الربا. ولهذا قلنا في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَدًا﴾ [النور: 4] إن النهي يعدم الوصف من شهادته، وهو الأداء، ويبقي الأصل، فيصير فاسداً. ومنها: صوم يوم العيد وأيام التشريق حسن مشروع بأصله، وهو الإمساك لله تعالى في وقته طاعة وقربة، قبيح بوصفه، وهو الإعراض عن الضيافة الموضوعة في هذا الوقت بالصوم، فلم تنقلب الطاعة معصية، بل طاعة انضم إليها وصف هو معصية. ألا ترى أن الصوم يقوم بالوقت ولا فساد فيه، والنهي يتعلق بوصفه، وهو أنه يوم عيد، فصار فاسداً. ومعنى الفاسد ما هو غير مشروع بوصفه، مثل الفاسد من الجواهر. وبيانه على وجه يعقل: أن الناس أضياف الله تعالى يوم العيد، فترك الشهوات بأصله طيب بوصفه، فصار تركه طاعة بأصله، معصية بوصفه على مثال البيع الفاسد. ولهذا صح النذر به؛ لأنه نذر بالطاعة، وإنما وصف المعصية متصل بذاته فعلاً، لا باسمه ذكراً. ولهذا قلنا في ظاهر الرواية: لا يلزم بالشروع؛ لأن الشروع فيه متصل بالمعصية، فأمر بالقطع حقاً لصاحب الشرع، فصار مضافاً إلى صاحب الشرع، ويرى العبد عن عهدته. ومنها: الصلاة وقت طلوع الشمس ودلوكها: مشروعة بأصلها، إذ لا قبح في أركانها وشروطها، والوقت صحيح بأصله، فاسد بوصفه، وهو أنه منسوب إلى الشيطان، كما جاءت به السنة، إلا أن الصلاة لا توجد
Among them: that selling wine is prohibited by its description, which is the price; because wine is property that is not mutqawwam, so it is suitable as a price from one aspect and not from another, thus it becomes fasid, not batil, and there is no defect in the pillar of the contract nor in its subject matter: so it becomes ugly by its description, legitimate in its root. Similarly, if one buys wine with a slave; because each one is a price for the other, so the contract is not concluded in the wine due to lack of its subject matter, and it is concluded in the slave due to the existence of its subject matter, and it becomes fasid due to the corruption of its price. Unlike a dead animal; because it is not property nor mutqawwam, so the sale occurs without a price, and it is not legitimate. Similarly, the skin of a dead animal; because it is not property nor mutqawwam. Similarly, a riba sale is legitimate in its root, which is the existence of its pillar in its subject matter, not legitimate in its description, which is the excess in the consideration, so it becomes fasid, not batil. Similarly, a corrupt condition in a sale: like riba. For this reason we said regarding the verse of Allah: {And never accept their testimony} (Quran 24:4) that the prohibition removes the description from their testimony, which is the performance, and preserves the root, so it becomes fasid. Among them: fasting on the day of Eid and the days of tashriq is good, legitimate in its root, which is refraining for Allah in its time as obedience and worship, ugly in its description, which is turning away from the hospitality established at this time by fasting, so obedience did not turn into disobedience, rather obedience to which a description that is disobedience became attached. Do you not see that the fasting exists in the time and there is no corruption in it, and the prohibition is attached to its description, which is that it is the day of Eid, so it becomes fasid. And the meaning of fasid is what is not legitimate by its description, like the defective among jewels. And its explanation in a reasonable manner: that people are guests of Allah on the day of Eid, refraining from desires by its root is good by its description, so its refraining becomes obedience by its root, disobedience by its description on the model of the corrupt sale. For this reason, a vow to fast it is valid; because it is a vow of obedience, and the description of disobedience is attached to its actual essence, not to its noun as a mention. For this reason we said in the apparent narration: it is not binding by commencement; because the commencement in it is connected to disobedience, so he was commanded to break it as a right of the Lawgiver, so it becomes attributed to the Lawgiver, and the servant is released from his responsibility. Among them: prayer at the time of sunrise and its zenith: it is legitimate in its root, since there is no ugliness in its pillars and conditions, and the time is valid in its root, corrupt in its description, which is that it is attributed to the devil, as has come in the Sunnah, except that prayer does not exist
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule exposition explaining the distinction between fasid (corrupt) and batil (void) based on whether the prohibition targets the essence (asl) or a description (wasf). The author, al-Bazdawi, uses multiple fiqh examples to illustrate that when a prohibition concerns a description (e.g., wine as a price, riba excess, fasting on Eid, prayer at sunrise), the act remains valid in its root but becomes corrupt due to that description, hence fasid rather than batil. He contrasts this with cases like selling a dead animal, which is batil because the subject matter itself lacks legal value. The principle is applied to Quranic testimony (Quran 24:4) and to acts of worship, emphasizing that a vow to fast on Eid is valid because the root is obedience, even though the description includes disobedience. The passage concludes with prayer at sunrise, noting its validity in root but corruption in description due to its association with shaitan.

Key Terms
الفاسد (al-fāsid): That which is legitimate in its root but prohibited in its description
الأصل (al-aṣl): The fundamental essence or pillar of an act or contract
الوصف (al-waṣf): An attribute or quality attached to an act that may attract prohibition
الباطل (al-bāṭil): That which is void ab initio due to a defect in its root

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is selling wine considered fasid and not batil?
A) Because wine is not property at all.
B) Because the prohibition is on the description (wine as a price), while the contract's root is valid.
C) Because the contract lacks a valid subject matter.
D) Because both parties are sinful.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: a prohibition on a description (wasf) yields fasid (corrupt), not batil (void); the root (asl) remains valid.

The Principle of an Act Being Good in Origin but Invalid Due to an Attribute (Wasf)
Explains the usul principle of asl-wasf with examples and hadith support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that an act valid in origin can be invalid due to a prohibited attribute, by distinguishing the asl from the wasf in a given case.

Core Idea
An act can be obedience in origin but become invalid due to a forbidden attribute attached to its performance.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every act that is essentially good remains valid when performed. Sometimes a prohibited attribute (wasf) attaches to the act, making it invalid (fasid) while its origin remains obedience. This lesson unpacks that distinction using fasting on Eid and prayer at prohibited times as key examples, drawing on a hadith about sunrise prayer. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly deriving rulings when multiple aspects combine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
First, isolate the essential act itself, without considering any temporal or circumstantial attributes. For example, the act of fasting or prayer is originally obedience (ta'a), legislated and good.
2
Identify the extrinsic attribute (wasf)
Next, determine the specific attribute that has been attached to the act, such as performing it on the day of Eid or at sunrise. This attribute is the subject of a prohibition (nahy).
The attribute is external to the act's essence (asl).
3
Distinguish between asl and wasf in ruling
The ruling applies to the combined act. The essence remains obedience, but the attribute renders the act invalid or deficient. The act does not become a sin; it becomes legally ineffective for fulfilling the obligation or supererogation.
Example: fasting on Eid is fasid because the attribute (Eid) is prohibited, but the fast itself is not sinful in origin.
4
Apply the distinction to the cases in the text
Work through the two cases: fasting on Eid (invalid due to description) and prayer at sunrise (deficient, not invalid, because time is a container not a measure). Note how the author contrasts them.
Prayer at sunrise is naqis (deficient) because the time is a container, not a cause; fasting is fasid because the time is a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمساك الله تعالى في وقته طاعةً وقُربةً قبيح بوصفه، وهو الإعراض عن الضيافة الموضوعة في هذا الوقت بالصوم، فلم تنقلب الطاعة معصية، بل طاعة انضم إليها وصف هو معصية. ألا يُرى أن الصوم يقوم بالوقت ولا فساد فيه، والنهي يتعلق بوصفه، وهو أنه يوم عيد، فصار فاسداً. والمتناول: ومعنى الفاسد ما هو غير مشروع بوصفه، مثل الفاسد من الجواهر. وبيانه على وجهِ يُعقَل : أن الناس أضياف الله تعالى يوم العيد، من جنس الشهوات بأصله طيب بوصفه، فصار تركه طاعةً بأصله، معصية بوصفه على مثال البيع الفاسد. ولهذا صح النذر به ؛ لأنه نذر بالطاعة، وإنما وَصَفُ المعصية متصل بذاته فعلاً، لا باسمه ذكراً. ولهذا قلنا في ظاهر قُبحَ في أركانها وشروطها، والوقت صحيح بأصله، فاسد بوصفه، وهو أنه منسوب إلى الشيطان، كما جاءت به السنة ) ، إلا أن الصلاة لا توجد بالوقت ؛ لأنه ظرفها لا معيارها وهو سيبها ، فصارت الصلاة ناقصة، لا فاسدة. فقيل : لا يُتأدَّى به الكامل، وتُضمن بالشروع، والصوم يقوم بالوقت، و ذكر حديث: عن عمرو بن عَبَسَة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: صل صلاة الصبح ثم أقصر عن الصلاة حين تطلع الشمس حتى ترتفع، فإنها تطلع حين تطلع بين قرني الشيطان، وحينئذ يسجد لها الكفار، ثم صل فإن الصلاة مشهودة محضورة حتى يستقل الظل بالرمح، ثم أقصر عن الصلاة، فإنه حينئذ تُسجّر جهنم فإذا أقبل الفيء فصل، فإن الصلاة مشهودة محضورة حتى تصلي العصر، ثم أقصر عن الصلاة حتى تغرب الشمس، فإنها تغرب بين قرني شيطان، وحينئذ يسجد لها الكفار. رواه أحمد ومسلم وأبو داود. وفي لفظه: ثم أقصر عن الصلاة حتى تطلع الشمس، فترتفع قيد رمح، أو رمحين، فإنها تطلع بين قرني شيطان فيصلي لها الكفار، ثم صل ما شئت، فإن الصلاة مشهودة مكتوبة حتى يعدل الرمح ظلَّه، ثم أقصر فإن جهنم تُسجر وتفتح أبوابها، فإذا زاغت الشمس فصل ما شئت فإن الصلاة مشهودة حتى تصلي العصر. ثم أقصر حتى تغرب الشمس، فإنها تغرب بين قرني شيطان، ويصلي لها الكفار. ولفظ النسائي: فإن الصلاة محضورة مشهودة إلى طلوع الشمس، فإنها تطلع بين قرني الشيطان، وهي ساعة صلاة الكفار، فدع الصلاة حتى ترتفع قيد رمح، ويذهب شعاعُها، ثم الصلاة محضورة مشهودة حتى تعتدل الشمس اعتدال الرمح بنصف النهار، فإنها ساعة تُفتّح فيها أبواب جهنم وتُسجِّجر، فدع الصلاة حتى يفيء الفيء، ثم الصلاة محضورة مشهودة حتى تغيب الشمس، فإنها تغيب بين قرني الشيطان، وهي صلاة الكفار. وعن عبد الله الصنابحي رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: إن الشمس تطلع ومعها قرن الشيطان فإذا ارتفعت، فارقها، فإذا استوت قارنها فإذا زالت فارقها فإذا دنت للغروب، قارنها، فإذا غربت فارقها. ونهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الصلاة في تلك الساعات، أخرجه مالك في الموطأ، والنسائي.
Fasting in its time is obedience and worship, but ugly in its description: it is turning away from the hospitality set in this time by fasting. So obedience did not turn into sin, rather obedience to which a description that is sin is attached. Do you not see that fasting occurs in the time and there is no corruption in it, but the prohibition pertains to its description, that it is the day of Eid, so it became invalid. The intended meaning: the invalid is what is not legislated by its description, like the invalid from jewels. Its explanation in an intelligible way: that people are guests of Allah on the day of Eid, of the type of desires, good in origin by its description, so leaving it became obedience in origin, sin in description, on the example of an invalid sale. Hence, a vow for it is valid because it is a vow for obedience, while the description of sin is attached to its essence as an act, not by its name as a mention. Therefore we said in the apparent narration: it does not become binding upon entry, because entering it is connected to sin, so cutting off was commanded as a right of the Lawgiver, so it becomes attributed to the Lawgiver, and the servant is absolved of responsibility. And from these: prayer at the time of sunrise and mid-day is legislated in its origin, for there is no ugliness in its pillars and conditions, and the time is valid by its origin, invalid by its description, that it is attributed to the devil, as established in the Sunnah, except that prayer does not exist by the time because it is its container, not its measure and its cause, so the prayer becomes deficient, not invalid. Thus it is said: the perfect prayer is not performed by it, and it is guaranteed by entry, while fasting occurs by the time… And mention the hadith: from Amr ibn Abasa that the Prophet [SAW] said: Pray the morning prayer, then refrain from prayer when the sun rises until it rises fully, for it rises between the two horns of the devil, and then the disbelievers prostrate to it, then pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until the shadow of the spear shortens, then refrain from prayer, for then Hell is kindled, then when the shadow returns, pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended until you pray Asr, then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of a devil, and then the disbelievers prostrate to it. Reported by Ahmad, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. In its wording: then refrain from prayer until the sun rises and rises a spear's length or two, for it rises between the horns of a devil and the disbelievers pray to it, then pray as you wish, for the prayer is witnessed and written until the spear's shadow equals it, then refrain, for Hell is kindled and its gates are opened, then when the sun declines, pray as you wish, for the prayer is witnessed until you pray Asr. Then refrain until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of a devil, and the disbelievers pray to it. And the wording of Nasa'i: Indeed the prayer is present and witnessed until sunrise, for it rises between the horns of the devil, and that is the hour of the prayer of the disbelievers, so leave prayer until it rises a spear's length and its rays disappear, then the prayer is present and witnessed until the sun becomes straight like a spear at midday, for that is an hour when the gates of Hell are opened and it is kindled, so leave prayer until the shadow returns, then prayer is present and witnessed until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of the devil, and that is the prayer of the disbelievers. And from Abdullah al-Sanabihi [RA] that the Messenger of Allah [SAW] said: The sun rises and with it is a horn of the devil, when it rises he separates from it, when it is at its zenith he accompanies it, when it declines he separates from it, when it approaches setting he accompanies it, when it sets he separates from it. And the Messenger of Allah [SAW] forbade prayer during those hours. Recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta and Nasa'i.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage explains a key usul principle: an act can be essentially good (e.g., fasting or prayer) but become invalid (fasid) due to a forbidden attribute (wasf) attached to its performance, such as fasting on the day of Eid or praying at sunrise. The author clarifies that the act itself remains obedience in origin, but the description (like 'Eid day' or 'time of shaitan') renders it invalid. He distinguishes between the act's essence (asl) and its attribute (wasf). For fasting on Eid, the prohibition pertains to the description, not the essence, so the fast is invalid (fasid) but not sinful in origin. This is why a vow to fast on Eid is valid (because the essence is obedience) but the fast itself is invalid. The author notes that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), it is not binding to continue if one starts (because starting involves sin), so the Lawgiver commands to break it. For prayer at prohibited times, the author contrasts with fasting: prayer is not inherently invalid at those times but becomes deficient (naqis) because the time is not a proper measure/cause for prayer (it is merely a container). Thus, the prayer is deficient, not invalid, so if one prays, it is valid but not complete and requires guarantee? The text then provides a long hadith about the association of certain times with the devil, supporting the prohibition of prayer at those times.

Key Terms
الوصف (al-wasf): الصفة العارضة للفعل التي توجب الحكم، ككون الفعل في يوم عيد أو وقت طلوع الشمس
الفاسد (al-fasid): ما كان مشروعاً بأصله غير مشروع بوصفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the vow is for the essence of fasting, which is obedience, not for the attribute of Eid.
B) Because the vow itself is an act of worship that overrides the prohibition.
C) Because fasting on Eid is actually recommended.
D) Because the prohibition of fasting on Eid is not established.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between an act's inherent goodness and the ruling of its performance when a prohibited attribute is attached: the act remains obedience in origin but becomes invalid (fasid) or deficient (naqis) due to the description.
