Division of Prohibition (Nahy) According to the Attribute of Ugliness (Qubh)
Classifying forbidden acts by the source of ugliness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify prohibited acts into four categories based on the attribute of ugliness (qubh) and distinguish between sensory and legal acts regarding their prohibition.

Core Idea
Prohibition is not uniform: acts are ugly either intrinsically or due to an external factor, affecting both validity and sinfulness.

In Hanafi usul, the prohibition (nahy) is divided according to the attribute of ugliness (qubh). This classification helps determine whether a prohibited act is inherently void or valid but sinful. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for distinguishing between sensory acts (like kufr) and legal acts (like contracts) in the eyes of the Sharī‘a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two broad categories of ugliness
Ugliness (qubh) can be intrinsic (li-‘aynihi), where the act itself is repellent, or extrinsic (li-ma‘nan fī ghayrihī), where an external factor makes it ugly.
Intrinsic ugliness is further divided into by convention (wad‘an) and by law (shar‘an).
2
Subdivide intrinsic ugliness
Intrinsic ugliness includes: (1) by convention, e.g., kufr, lying, frivolity; and (2) by law, e.g., selling a free person, which is annexed to the first because both are inherently void.
Acts that are ugly by law are void because they are not the proper locus for the legal act.
3
Subdivide extrinsic ugliness
Extrinsic ugliness includes: (1) plain, e.g., sale during Friday adhan or prayer in usurped land; and (2) annexed in description, e.g., corrupt (fasid) sale or fasting on the day of sacrifice.
The annexed category behaves like intrinsic ugliness in some respects, e.g., the prohibition applies to the act itself.
4
Apply the classification to sensory and legal acts
Prohibition of sensory acts (like physical movements) falls under intrinsic ugliness categories. Prohibition of legal acts (like contracts) falls under the extrinsic category annexed in description, meaning the act is valid but the prohibition attaches.
This distinction explains why some prohibited acts (e.g., sale during adhan) are valid in contract but sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقط وصفُ التراب، فكذلك يُهدَر وصف الزنا بالحرمة؛ لقيامه مقام ما لا يوصف بذلك في إيجاب حرمة المصاهرة.
وأما سفر المعصية : فغير منهي لمعنى فيه؛ لأنه من حيث إنه خروج مديدٌ مباح، وإنما العصيان في فعل قطع الطريق، أو التمرد على المولى، وهو مجاور له، فكان كالبيع وقت النداء.
ولا يلزم على هذا النهي عن الأفعال الحسية؛ لأن القول بكمال القبح فيها، وهو مقتضى مع كمال المقصود، ممكن، على ما قلنا.
والنهي في صفة القبح ينقسم انقسام الأمر :
- ما قبح لعينه وضعاً، مثل الكفر، والكذب، والعبث.
- وما قبح لعينه شرعاً مُلحقاً بالقسم الأول، وهو بيعُ الحُرِّ، والمضامين، والملاقيح؛ لأن البيع لما وضع لتمليك المال: كان باطلاً في غير محله.
- وما قبح لمعنى في غيره، وهو البيع وقت النداء، والصلاة في أرض مغصوبة.
- وما قبح لمعنى في غيره، وهو ملحق به وصفاً، وذلك مثل البيع الفاسد، وصيام يوم النحر.
والأمور
والنهي عن الأفعال الحسية : يقع على القسم الأول، وعن الشرعية : يقعُ على هذا القسم، الذي قلنا إنه ملحق به وصفاً، والله أعلم.
And the description of earth [in tayammum] falls away, so likewise the description of zina by sanctity is disregarded; because it stands in the place of what is not described by that in causing the sanctity of marriage. As for the journey of disobedience: it is not prohibited for a meaning within it; because it is from the aspect that it is an extended departure that is permissible, and disobedience is only in the act of cutting the road or rebelling against the master, and it is adjacent to it, so it becomes like the sale at the time of the call [to prayer]. And this does not necessitate prohibition of sensory acts; because saying that ugliness is complete in them, and it is required along with the completeness of the purpose, is possible, as we said. And the prohibition regarding the attribute of ugliness divides like the division of command: what is ugly in essence by convention, like disbelief, lying, and frivolity; and what is ugly in essence by law, annexed to the first category, namely selling a free person, and [selling] what is guaranteed [by law] and what is in the wombs of animals; because when sale was instituted for ownership of property, it is void in other than its place. And what is ugly for a meaning in other than it, namely the sale at the time of the call, and prayer in usurped land. And what is ugly for a meaning in other than it, but annexed to it in description, such as the corrupt sale and fasting on the day of sacrifice. And the matters [remainder?] And the prohibition of sensory acts falls on the first category, and of legal acts falls on this category, which we said is annexed to it in description, and God knows best.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a legal definition and classification of the types of prohibition (nahy) based on the attribute of ugliness (qubh). The author begins with previous examples: the description of earth in tayammum is dropped, similarly the description of zina by sanctity is disregarded because it stands in place of something not so described in causing the sanctity of marriage. Then, a journey of disobedience is not prohibited for a meaning within itself because it is intrinsically permissible travel; the disobedience lies in the accompanying act (like highway robbery or rebellion against the master), so it is like a sale during the Friday call (which is prohibited due to an external factor). The author argues that this does not necessitate prohibition of sensory acts because it is possible to assert complete ugliness in them along with complete purpose. The main classification: prohibition divides like command (amr). First, what is inherently ugly by convention (wad'an) such as kufr, kadhb, and 'abath (play). Second, what is inherently ugly by law (shar'an) and annexed to the first, such as selling a free person, or selling what is guaranteed (like a runaway slave who is guaranteed) and what is in the wombs (malaqih); because sale is based on ownership of property, so it is void when applied to non-property. Third, what is ugly due to something external, like sale during the Friday adhan or prayer in usurped land. Fourth, what is ugly due to something external but annexed in description to the first category, like a fasid (defective) sale or fasting on the day of sacrifice. Finally, the prohibition of sensory acts (like physical actions) applies to the first category, while the prohibition of legal acts (like contracts) applies to the fourth category (annexed in description). This classification is based on rational analysis of the causes of ugliness.

Key Terms
القبح (al-qubh): Ugliness or repulsiveness of an act, which is the basis for prohibition. It can be intrinsic (li-'aynihi) or extrinsic (li-ghairihi).
ما قبح لعينه وضعاً (ma qubuha li-'aynihi wad'an): What is inherently ugly by convention, such as kufr, lying, and frivolity; its prohibition is based on the very nature of the act.
ما قبح لمعنى في غيره (ma qubuha li-ma'nan fi ghairihi): What is ugly due to a meaning outside itself, such as a sale during the Friday adhan or prayer in usurped land; the act itself is permissible but becomes prohibited due to an external factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification of prohibition (nahy), which of the following is an example of something ugly due to a meaning outside itself (ما قبح لمعنى في غيره)?
A) Kufr (disbelief)
B) Lying
C) Selling a free person
D) Prayer in usurped land

Key Takeaway
The division of prohibition according to ugliness distinguishes between acts that are intrinsically void and those that are valid but sinful, a critical nuance for Hanafi fiqh and fatwa.
